 <p align="CENTER"><font size="-1" color="GREEN"><a href="index.htm"><img src="img/tease.jpg"></a><br><i>The Canterbury Tales and Other Works of Chaucer (Middle English)</i>, by Geoffery Chaucer, [14th cent.], at sacred-texts.com</font></p><hr> <h4 align="center">The Romaunt of the Rose</h4> <h3 align="center">Fragment B</h3> <a name="an_1706"></a> Whanne I hadde smelled the savour swote,<br> <a name="an_1707"></a> No will hadde I fro thens yit goo,<br> <a name="an_1708"></a> Bot somdell neer it wente I thoo,<br> <a name="an_1709"></a> To take it, but myn hond, for drede,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1710">1710</a></font></span> Ne dorste I to the Rose bede<br> <a name="an_1711"></a> For thesteles sharpe, of many maneres,<br> <a name="an_1712"></a> Netles, thornes, and hokede breres,<br> <a name="an_1713"></a> For mych they distourbled me,<br> <a name="an_1714"></a> For sore I dradde to harmed be.<br> <a name="an_1715"></a> The God of Love, with bowe bent,<br> <a name="an_1716"></a> That all day set hadde his talent<br> <a name="an_1717"></a> To pursuen and to spien me,<br> <a name="an_1718"></a> Was stondyng by a fige-tree.<br> <a name="an_1719"></a> And whanne he saw hou that I<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1720">1720</a></font></span> Hadde chosen so ententifly<br> <a name="an_1721"></a> The botoun, more unto my pay<br> <a name="an_1722"></a> Than ony other that I say,<br> <a name="an_1723"></a> He tok an arowe full sharply whet,<br> <a name="an_1724"></a> And in his bowe whanne it was set,<br> <a name="an_1725"></a> He streight up to his ere drough<br> <a name="an_1726"></a> The stronge bowe that was so tough,<br> <a name="an_1727"></a> And shet att me so wondir smerte<br> <a name="an_1728"></a> That thorough myn ye unto myn herte<br> <a name="an_1729"></a> The takel smot, and depe it wente.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1730">1730</a></font></span> And therwithall such cold me hente<br> <a name="an_1731"></a> That under clothes warme and softe<br> <a name="an_1732"></a> Sithen that day I have chevered ofte.<br> <a name="an_1733"></a> Whanne I was hurt thus, in [a] stounde<br> <a name="an_1734"></a> I felle doun plat unto the grounde.<br> <a name="an_1735"></a> Myn herte failed and feynted ay,<br> <a name="an_1736"></a> And longe tyme a-swoone I lay.<br> <a name="an_1737"></a> But whanne I come out of swonyng,<br> <a name="an_1738"></a> And hadde witt and my felyng,<br> <a name="an_1739"></a> I was all maat, and wende full well<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1740">1740</a></font></span> Of blood have loren a full gret dell.<br> <a name="an_1741"></a> But certes, the arowe that in me stod<br> <a name="an_1742"></a> Of me ne drew no drope of blod,<br> <a name="an_1743"></a> For-why I found my wounde all dreie.<br> <a name="an_1744"></a> Thanne tok I with myn hondis tweie<br> <a name="an_1745"></a> The arowe, and ful fast out it plighte,<br> <a name="an_1746"></a> And in the pullyng sore I sighte.<br> <a name="an_1747"></a> So at the last the shaft of tree<br> <a name="an_1748"></a> I drough out with the fethers thre.<br> <a name="an_1749"></a> But yet the hokede heed, ywis,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1750">1750</a></font></span> The which [that] Beaute callid is,<br> <a name="an_1751"></a> Gan so depe in myn herte passe,<br> <a name="an_1752"></a> That I it myghte nought arace;<br> <a name="an_1753"></a> But in myn herte still it stod,<br> <a name="an_1754"></a> Al bledde I not a drope of blod.<br> <a name="an_1755"></a> I was bothe anguyssous and trouble<br> <a name="an_1756"></a> For the perill that I saw double:<br> <a name="an_1757"></a> I nyste what to seye or do,<br> <a name="an_1758"></a> Ne gete a leche my woundis to;<br> <a name="an_1759"></a> For neithir thurgh gras ne rote<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1760">1760</a></font></span> Ne hadde I help of hope ne bote.<br> <a name="an_1761"></a> But to the botoun evermo<br> <a name="an_1762"></a> Myn herte drew, for all my wo;<br> <a name="an_1763"></a> My thought was in noon other thing,<br> <a name="an_1764"></a> For hadde it ben in my kepyng,<br> <a name="an_1765"></a> It wolde have brought my lyf agayn.<br> <a name="an_1766"></a> For certis evenly, I dar wel seyn,<br> <a name="an_1767"></a> The sight oonly and the savour<br> <a name="an_1768"></a> Alegged mych of my langour.<br> <a name="an_1769"></a> Thanne gan I for to drawe me<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1770">1770</a></font></span> Toward the botoun faire to se;<br> <a name="an_1771"></a> And Love hadde gete hym, in a throwe,<br> <a name="an_1772"></a> Another arowe into his bowe,<br> <a name="an_1773"></a> And for to shete gan hym dresse.<br> <a name="an_1774"></a> The arowis name was Symplesse,<br> <a name="an_1775"></a> And whanne that Love gan nygh me nere,<br> <a name="an_1776"></a> He drow it up, withouten were,<br> <a name="an_1777"></a> And shet at me with all his myght,<br> <a name="an_1778"></a> So that this arowe anoon-right<br> <a name="an_1779"></a> Thourghout [myn] eigh, as it was founde,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1780">1780</a></font></span> Into myn herte hath maad a wounde.<br> <a name="an_1781"></a> Thanne I anoon dide al my craft<br> <a name="an_1782"></a> For to drawen out the shaft,<br> <a name="an_1783"></a> And therwithall I sighed eft.<br> <a name="an_1784"></a> But in myn herte the heed was left,<br> <a name="an_1785"></a> Which ay encreside my desir<br> <a name="an_1786"></a> Unto the botoun drawe ner;<br> <a name="an_1787"></a> And evermo that me was woo,<br> <a name="an_1788"></a> The more desir hadde I to goo<br> <a name="an_1789"></a> Unto the roser, where that grew<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1790">1790</a></font></span> The freysshe botoun so bright of hew.<br> <a name="an_1791"></a> Betir me were to have laten be,<br> <a name="an_1792"></a> But it bihovede nedes me<br> <a name="an_1793"></a> To don right as myn herte bad,<br> <a name="an_1794"></a> For evere the body must be lad<br> <a name="an_1795"></a> Aftir the herte, in wele and woo;<br> <a name="an_1796"></a> Of force togidre they must goo.<br> <a name="an_1797"></a> But never this archer wolde feyne<br> <a name="an_1798"></a> To shete at me with all his peyne,<br> <a name="an_1799"></a> And for to make me to hym mete.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1800">1800</a></font></span> The thridde arowe he gan to shete,<br> <a name="an_1801"></a> Whanne best his tyme he myght espie,<br> <a name="an_1802"></a> The which was named Curtesie.<br> <a name="an_1803"></a> Into myn herte it dide avale;<br> <a name="an_1804"></a> A-swoone I fell bothe deed and pale.<br> <a name="an_1805"></a> Long tyme I lay and stired nought,<br> <a name="an_1806"></a> Till I abraide out of my thought,<br> <a name="an_1807"></a> And faste thanne I avysede me<br> <a name="an_1808"></a> To drawe out the shaft of tree.<br> <a name="an_1809"></a> But evere the heed was left bihynde,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1810">1810</a></font></span> For ought I couth. pulle or wynde,<br> <a name="an_1811"></a> So sore it stikid whanne I was hit,<br> <a name="an_1812"></a> That by no craft I myght it flit.<br> <a name="an_1813"></a> But anguyssous and full of thought,<br> <a name="an_1814"></a> I felte sich woo my wounde ay wrought,<br> <a name="an_1815"></a> That somonede me alway to goo<br> <a name="an_1816"></a> Toward the Rose that plesede me soo,<br> <a name="an_1817"></a> But I ne durste in no maner,<br> <a name="an_1818"></a> Bicause the archer was so ner.<br> <a name="an_1819"></a> "For evermore gladly," as I rede,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1820">1820</a></font></span> "Brent child of fir hath myche drede."<br> <a name="an_1821"></a> And, certis yit, for al my peyne,<br> <a name="an_1822"></a> Though that I sigh yit arwis reyne,<br> <a name="an_1823"></a> And grounde quarels sharpe of steell,<br> <a name="an_1824"></a> Ne for no payne that I myght feell,<br> <a name="an_1825"></a> Yit myght I not mysilf witholde<br> <a name="an_1826"></a> The faire roser to biholde,<br> <a name="an_1827"></a> For Love me yaf sich hardement<br> <a name="an_1828"></a> For to fulfille his comaundement.<br> <a name="an_1829"></a> Upon my fete I ros up than,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1830">1830</a></font></span> Feble as a forwoundid man,<br> <a name="an_1831"></a> And forth to gon [my] myght I sette,<br> <a name="an_1832"></a> And for the archer nolde I lette.<br> <a name="an_1833"></a> Toward the roser fast I drow,<br> <a name="an_1834"></a> But thornes sharpe mo than ynow<br> <a name="an_1835"></a> Ther were, and also thisteles thikke,<br> <a name="an_1836"></a> And breres, brymme for to prikke,<br> <a name="an_1837"></a> That I ne myghte gete grace<br> <a name="an_1838"></a> The rowe thornes for to passe,<br> <a name="an_1839"></a> To sen the roses fresshe of hewe.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1840">1840</a></font></span> I must abide, though it me rewe,<br> <a name="an_1841"></a> The hegge aboute so thikke was,<br> <a name="an_1842"></a> That closide the roses in compas.<br> <a name="an_1843"></a> But o thing lyked me right well:<br> <a name="an_1844"></a> I was so nygh, I myghte fel<br> <a name="an_1845"></a> Of the botoun the swote odour,<br> <a name="an_1846"></a> And also se the fresshe colour,<br> <a name="an_1847"></a> And that right gretly liked me,<br> <a name="an_1848"></a> That I so neer myghte it se.<br> <a name="an_1849"></a> Sich joie anoon therof hadde I<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1850">1850</a></font></span> That I forgat my malady.<br> <a name="an_1851"></a> To sen I hadde sich delit,<br> <a name="an_1852"></a> Of sorwe and angre I was al quyt,<br> <a name="an_1853"></a> And of my woundes that I hadde thore;<br> <a name="an_1854"></a> For nothing liken me myght more<br> <a name="an_1855"></a> Than dwellen by the roser ay,<br> <a name="an_1856"></a> And thennes never to passe away.<br> <a name="an_1857"></a> But whanne a while I hadde be thar,<br> <a name="an_1858"></a> The God of Love, which al toshar<br> <a name="an_1859"></a> Myn herte with his arwis kene,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1860">1860</a></font></span> Castith hym to yeve me woundis grene.<br> <a name="an_1861"></a> He shet at me full hastily<br> <a name="an_1862"></a> An arwe named Company,<br> <a name="an_1863"></a> The whiche takell is full able<br> <a name="an_1864"></a> To make these ladies merciable.<br> <a name="an_1865"></a> Thanne I anoon gan chaungen hewe<br> <a name="an_1866"></a> For grevaunce of my wounde newe,<br> <a name="an_1867"></a> That I agayn fell in swonyng<br> <a name="an_1868"></a> And sighede sore in compleynyng.<br> <a name="an_1869"></a> Soore I compleyned that my sore<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1870">1870</a></font></span> On me gan greven more and more.<br> <a name="an_1871"></a> I hadde noon hope of allegeaunce;<br> <a name="an_1872"></a> So nygh I drow to desperaunce,<br> <a name="an_1873"></a> I roughte of deth ne of lyf,<br> <a name="an_1874"></a> Wheder that Love wolde me dryf.<br> <a name="an_1875"></a> Yf me a martir wolde he make,<br> <a name="an_1876"></a> I myght his power nought forsake.<br> <a name="an_1877"></a> And while for anger thus I wok,<br> <a name="an_1878"></a> The God of Love an arowe tok --<br> <a name="an_1879"></a> Ful sharp it was and pugnaunt --<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1880">1880</a></font></span> And it was callid Faire-Semblaunt,<br> <a name="an_1881"></a> The which in no wise wole consente<br> <a name="an_1882"></a> That ony lover hym repente<br> <a name="an_1883"></a> To serve his love with herte and alle,<br> <a name="an_1884"></a> For ony perill that may bifalle.<br> <a name="an_1885"></a> But though this arwe was kene grounde<br> <a name="an_1886"></a> As ony rasour that is founde,<br> <a name="an_1887"></a> To kutte and kerve, at the poynt<br> <a name="an_1888"></a> The God of Love it hadde anoynt<br> <a name="an_1889"></a> With a precious oynement,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1890">1890</a></font></span> Somdell to yeve aleggement<br> <a name="an_1891"></a> Upon the woundes that he had<br> <a name="an_1893"></a> To helpe her sores, and to cure,<br> <a name="an_1894"></a> And that they may the bet endure.<br> <a name="an_1895"></a> But yit this arwe, withoute more,<br> <a name="an_1896"></a> Made in myn herte a large sore,<br> <a name="an_1897"></a> That in full gret peyne I abod.<br> <a name="an_1898"></a> But ay the oynement wente abrod;<br> <a name="an_1899"></a> Thourghout my woundes large and wide<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1900">1900</a></font></span> It spredde aboute in every side,<br> <a name="an_1901"></a> Thorough whos vertu and whos myght<br> <a name="an_1902"></a> Myn herte joyfull was and light.<br> <a name="an_1903"></a> I hadde ben deed and al toshent,<br> <a name="an_1904"></a> But for the precious oynement.<br> <a name="an_1905"></a> The shaft I drow out of the arwe,<br> <a name="an_1906"></a> Rokyng for wo right wondir narwe;<br> <a name="an_1907"></a> But the heed, which made me smerte,<br> <a name="an_1908"></a> Lefte bihynde in myn herte<br> <a name="an_1909"></a> With other foure, I dar wel say,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1910">1910</a></font></span> That never wole be take away.<br> <a name="an_1911"></a> But the oynement halp me wel,<br> <a name="an_1912"></a> And yit sich sorwe dide I fel<br> <a name="an_1913"></a> That al day I chaunged hewe<br> <a name="an_1914"></a> Of my woundes fresshe and newe,<br> <a name="an_1915"></a> As men myght se in my visage.<br> <a name="an_1916"></a> The arwis were so full of rage,<br> <a name="an_1917"></a> So variaunt of diversitee,<br> <a name="an_1918"></a> That men in everich myghte se<br> <a name="an_1919"></a> Bothe gret anoy and eke swetnesse,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1920">1920</a></font></span> And joie meynt with bittirnesse.<br> <a name="an_1921"></a> Now were they esy, now were they wod;<br> <a name="an_1922"></a> In hem I felte bothe harm and good;<br> <a name="an_1923"></a> Now sore without alleggement,<br> <a name="an_1924"></a> Now softenyng with oynement;<br> <a name="an_1925"></a> It softnede heere and prikkith there:<br> <a name="an_1926"></a> Thus ese and anger togidre were.<br> <a name="an_1927"></a> The God of Love delyverly<br> <a name="an_1928"></a> Com lepande to me hastily,<br> <a name="an_1929"></a> And seide to me in gret rape,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1930">1930</a></font></span> "Yeld thee, for thou may not escape!<br> <a name="an_1931"></a> May no defence availe thee heer;<br> <a name="an_1932"></a> Therfore I rede make no daunger.<br> <a name="an_1933"></a> If thou wolt yelde thee hastily,<br> <a name="an_1934"></a> Thou shalt rather have mercy.<br> <a name="an_1935"></a> He is a fool in sikernesse,<br> <a name="an_1936"></a> That with daunger or stoutnesse<br> <a name="an_1937"></a> Rebellith there that he shulde plese;<br> <a name="an_1938"></a> In sich folye is litel ese.<br> <a name="an_1939"></a> Be meke where thou must nedis bow;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1940">1940</a></font></span> To stryve ageyn is nought thi prow.<br> <a name="an_1941"></a> Com at oones, and have ydoo,<br> <a name="an_1942"></a> For I wol that it be soo.<br> <a name="an_1943"></a> Thanne yeld thee heere debonairly."<br> <a name="an_1944"></a> And I answerid ful hombly,<br> <a name="an_1945"></a> "Gladly, sir, at youre biddyng,<br> <a name="an_1946"></a> I wole me yelde in alle thyng.<br> <a name="an_1947"></a> To youre servyse I wol me take,<br> <a name="an_1948"></a> For God defende that I shulde make<br> <a name="an_1949"></a> Ageyn youre biddyng resistence.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1950">1950</a></font></span> I wole not don so gret offence,<br> <a name="an_1951"></a> For if I dide, it were no skile.<br> <a name="an_1952"></a> Ye may do with me what ye wile,<br> <a name="an_1953"></a> Save or spille, and also sloo.<br> <a name="an_1954"></a> Fro you in no wise may I goo.<br> <a name="an_1955"></a> My lyf, my deth is in youre hond;<br> <a name="an_1956"></a> I may not laste out of youre bond.<br> <a name="an_1957"></a> Pleyn at youre lyst I yelde me,<br> <a name="an_1958"></a> Hopyng in herte that sumtyme ye<br> <a name="an_1959"></a> Comfort and ese shull me sende;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1960">1960</a></font></span> Or ellis, shortly, this is the eende,<br> <a name="an_1961"></a> Withouten helthe I mot ay dure,<br> <a name="an_1962"></a> But if ye take me to youre cure.<br> <a name="an_1963"></a> Comfort or helthe how shuld I have,<br> <a name="an_1964"></a> Sith ye me hurt, but ye me save?<br> <a name="an_1965"></a> The helthe of love mot be founde<br> <a name="an_1966"></a> Where as they token first her wounde.<br> <a name="an_1967"></a> And if ye lyst of me to make<br> <a name="an_1968"></a> Youre prisoner, I wol it take<br> <a name="an_1969"></a> Of herte and will, fully at gree.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1970">1970</a></font></span> Hoolly and pleyn Y yelde me,<br> <a name="an_1971"></a> Withoute feynyng or feyntise,<br> <a name="an_1972"></a> To be governed by youre emprise.<br> <a name="an_1973"></a> Of you I here so myche pris,<br> <a name="an_1974"></a> I wole ben hool at youre devis<br> <a name="an_1975"></a> For to fulfille youre lykyng<br> <a name="an_1976"></a> And repente for nothyng,<br> <a name="an_1977"></a> Hopyng to have yit in som tide<br> <a name="an_1978"></a> Mercy of that I abide."<br> <a name="an_1979"></a> And with that covenaunt yelde I me<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1980">1980</a></font></span> Anoon, down knelyng upon my kne,<br> <a name="an_1981"></a> Proferyng for to kisse his feet;<br> <a name="an_1982"></a> But for nothyng he wolde [me] let,<br> <a name="an_1983"></a> And seide, "I love thee bothe and preise,<br> <a name="an_1984"></a> Sen that thyn aunswar doth me ease,<br> <a name="an_1985"></a> For thou answerid so curteisly.<br> <a name="an_1986"></a> For now I wot wel uttirly<br> <a name="an_1987"></a> That thou art gentyll by thi speche.<br> <a name="an_1988"></a> For though a man fer wolde seche,<br> <a name="an_1989"></a> He shulde not fynden, in certeyn,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_1990">1990</a></font></span> No sich answer of no vileyn;<br> <a name="an_1991"></a> For sich a word ne myghte nought<br> <a name="an_1992"></a> Isse out of a vilayns thought.<br> <a name="an_1993"></a> Thou shalt not lesen of thi speche,<br> <a name="an_1994"></a> For [to] thy helpyng wole I eche,<br> <a name="an_1995"></a> And eke encresen that I may.<br> <a name="an_1996"></a> But first I wole that thou obay<br> <a name="an_1997"></a> Fully, for thyn avauntage,<br> <a name="an_1998"></a> Anoon to do was never couth<br> <a name="an_2001"></a> For to aproche it, ne for to touche;<br> <a name="an_2002"></a> For sauff of cherlis I ne vouche<br> <a name="an_2003"></a> That they shull never neigh it nere.<br> <a name="an_2004"></a> For curteis and of faire manere,<br> <a name="an_2005"></a> Well taught and ful of gentilnesse<br> <a name="an_2006"></a> He muste ben that shal me kysse,<br> <a name="an_2007"></a> And also of full high fraunchise,<br> <a name="an_2008"></a> That shal atteyne to that emprise.<br> <a name="an_2009"></a> And first of o thing warne I thee,<br> <span <a name="an_2045"></a> Of oon and other, where I have ben<br> <a name="an_2046"></a> Disceyved ofte, withouten wen.<br> <a name="an_2047"></a> These felouns, full of falsite,<br> <a class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2270">2270</a></font></span> How they come on or off ageyn.<br> <a name="an_2271"></a> Were streite gloves with awmenere<br> <a name="an_2272"></a> Of silk; and alwey with good chere<br> <a name="an_2273"></a> Thou yeve, if thou have richesse;<br> <a name="an_2274"></a> And if thou have nought, spende the lesse.<br> <a name="an_2275"></a> Alwey be mery, if thou may,<br> <a name="an_2276"></a> But waste not thi good alway.<br> <a name="an_2277"></a> Have hat of floures as fresh as May,<br> <a name="an_2278"></a> Chapelett of roses of Whitsonday,<br> <a name="an_2279"></a> For sich array ne costeth but lite.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2280">2280</a></font></span> Thyn hondis wassh, thy teeth make white,<br> <a name="an_2281"></a> And let no filthe upon thee bee.<br> <a name="an_2282"></a> Thy nailes blak if thou maist see,<br> <a name="an_2283"></a> Voide it awey delyverly,<br> <a name="an_2284"></a> And kembe thyn heed right jolily.<br> <a name="an_2285"></a> Fard not thi visage in no wise,<br> <a name="an_2286"></a> For that of love is not th' emprise;<br> <a name="an_2287"></a> For love doth haten, as I fynde,<br> <a name="an_2288"></a> A beaute that cometh not of kynde.<br> <a name="an_2289"></a> Alwey in herte I rede thee<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2290">2290</a></font></span> Glad and mery for to be,<br> <a name="an_2291"></a> And be as joyfull as thou can;<br> <a name="an_2292"></a> Love hath no joye of sorowful man.<br> <a name="an_2293"></a> That yvell is full of curtesie<br> <a name="an_2294"></a> That laughith in his maladie;<br> <a name="an_2295"></a> For ever of love the siknesse<br> <a name="an_2296"></a> Is meynd with swete and bitternesse.<br> <a name="an_2297"></a> The sore of love is merveilous;<br> <a name="an_2298"></a> For now the lover [is. joyous,<br> <a name="an_2299"></a> Now can he pleyne, now can he grone,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2300">2300</a></font></span> Now can he syngen, now maken mone;<br> <a name="an_2301"></a> To-day he pleyneth for hevynesse,<br> <a name="an_2302"></a> To-morowe he pleyeth for jolynesse.<br> <a name="an_2303"></a> The lyf of love is full contrarie,<br> <a name="an_2304"></a> Which stoundemele can ofte varie.<br> <a name="an_2305"></a> But if thou canst mirthis make,<br> <a name="an_2306"></a> That men in gre wole gladly take,<br> <a name="an_2307"></a> Do it goodly, I comaunde thee.<br> <a name="an_2308"></a> For men shulde, wheresoevere they be,<br> <a name="an_2309"></a> Do thing that hem sittyng is,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2310">2310</a></font></span> For therof cometh good loos and pris.<br> <a name="an_2311"></a> Whereof that thou be vertuous,<br> <a name="an_2312"></a> Ne be not straunge ne daungerous;<br> <a name="an_2313"></a> For if that thou good ridere be,<br> <a name="an_2314"></a> Prike gladly, that men may se.<br> <a name="an_2315"></a> In armes also if thou konne,<br> <a name="an_2316"></a> Pursue til thou a name hast wonne.<br> <a name="an_2317"></a> And color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2320">2320</a></font></span> It is thi worship for t' obeye.<br> <a name="an_2321"></a> Also to you it longith ay<br> <a name="an_2322"></a> To harpe and gitterne, daunce and play,<br> <a name="an_2323"></a> For if he can wel foote and daunce,<br> <a name="an_2324"></a> It may hym greetly do avaunce.<br> <a name="an_2325"></a> Among eke, for thy lady sake,<br> <a name="an_2326"></a> Songes and complayntes that thou make,<br> <a name="an_2327"></a> For that wole meven in hir herte,<br> <a name="an_2328"></a> Whanne they reden of thy smerte.<br> <a name="an_2331"></a> Resoun wole that a lover be<br> <a name="an_2332"></a> In his yiftes more large and fre<br> <a name="an_2333"></a> Than cherles that ben not of lovyng.<br> <a name="an_2334"></a> For who therof can ony thyng,<br> <a name="an_2335"></a> He shal be leef ay for to yeve,<br> <a name="an_2336"></a> In Loves lore whoso wolde leve;<br> <a name="an_2337"></a> For <a name="an_2346"></a> In wordis fewe compendiously,<br> <a name="an_2347"></a> That thou the better mayst on hem thynke,<br> <a name="an_2348"></a> Whether so it be thou wake or wynke.<br> <a name="an_2354"></a> And of largesse alosed be.<br> <a name="an_2355"></a> "First I joyne thee, heere in penaunce,<br> <a name="an_2356"></a> That evere, withoute repentaunce,<br> <a <a name="an_2373"></a> For if thou yevest it in lenyng,<br> <a name="an_2374"></a> I holde it but a wrecchid thyng;<br> <a name="an_2375"></a> Therfore yeve it hool and quyt,<br> <a <a name="an_2401"></a> Cotidien ne quarteyne,<br> <a name="an_2402"></a> It is nat so ful of peyne.<br> <a name="an_2403"></a> For often tymes it shal falle<br> <a name="an_2404"></a> In love, among name="an_2545"></a> If ony word thanne come to mynde<br> <a name="an_2546"></a> That thou to seye hast left bihynde,<br> <a name="an_2547"></a> Thanne thou shalt brenne in gret martir,<br> <a name="an_2548"></a> For thou shalt brenne as ony fir.<br> <a name="an_2549"></a> This is the stryf and eke the affray,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2550">2550</a></font></span> And the batell that lastith ay.<br> <a name="an_2551"></a> This bargeyn eende may never take,<br> <a name="an_2552"></a> But if that she thi pees will make.<br> <a name="an_2553"></a> And whanne the nyght is comen, anoon<br> <a name="an_2554"></a> A thousand angres shall come uppon.<br> <a name="an_2555"></a> To bedde as fast thou wolt thee dight,<br> <a name="an_2556"></a> Where thou shalt have but smal delit.<br> <a name="an_2557"></a> For whanne thou wenest for to slepe,<br> <a name="an_2558"></a> So full of peyne shalt thou crepe,<br> <a name="an_2559"></a> Sterte in thi bed aboute full wide,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2560">2560</a></font></span> And turne full ofte on every side,<br> <a name="an_2561"></a> Now dounward groff and now upright,<br> <a name="an_2562"></a> And walowe in woo the longe nyght.<br> <a name="an_2563"></a> Thine armys shalt thou sprede a-bred,<br> <a name="an_2564"></a> As man in werre were forwerreyd.<br> <a name="an_2565"></a> Thanne shall thee come a remembraunce<br> <a name="an_2566"></a> Of hir shap and hir semblaunce,<br> <a name="an_2567"></a> Whereto non other may be pere.<br> <a name="an_2568"></a> And wite thou wel, withoute were,<br> <a name="an_2569"></a> That thee shal se[me] somtyme that nyght<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2570">2570</a></font></span> That thou hast hir that is so bright<br> <a name="an_2571"></a> Naked bitwene thyne armes there,<br> <a name="an_2572"></a> All sothfastnesse as though it were.<br> <a name="an_2573"></a> Thou shalt make castels thanne in Spayne<br> <a name="an_2574"></a> And dreme of joye, all but in vayne,<br> <a name="an_2575"></a> And thee deliten of right nought,<br> <a name="an_2576"></a> While thou so slombrest in that thought<br> <a name="an_2577"></a> That is so swete and delitable,<br> <a name="an_2578"></a> The which, in soth, nys but fable,<br> <a name="an_2579"></a> For it ne shall no while laste.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2580">2580</a></font></span> Thanne shalt thou sighe and wepe faste,<br> <a name="an_2581"></a> And say, `Dere God, what thing is this?<br> <a name="an_2582"></a> My drem is turned all amys,<br> <a name="an_2583"></a> Which was full swete and apparent;<br> <a name="an_2584"></a> But now I wake, it is al shent!<br> <a name="an_2585"></a> Now yede this mery thought away!<br> <a name="an_2586"></a> Twenty tymes upon a day<br> <a name="an_2587"></a> I wolde this thought wolde come ageyn,<br> <a name="an_2588"></a> For it aleggith well my peyn.<br> <a name="an_2589"></a> It makith me full of joyfull thought;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2590">2590</a></font></span> It sleth me, that it lastith noght.<br> <a name="an_2591"></a> A, Lord! Why nyl ye me socoure<br> <a name="an_2592"></a> The joye, I trowe, that I langoure?<br> <a name="an_2593"></a> The deth I wolde me shulde sloo<br> <a name="an_2594"></a> While I lye in hir armes twoo.<br> <a name="an_2595"></a> Myn harm is hard, withouten wene;<br> <a name="an_2596"></a> My gret unese full ofte I meene.<br> <a name="an_2597"></a> "`But wolde Love do so I myght<br> <a name="an_2598"></a> Have fully joye of hir so bright,<br> <a name="an_2599"></a> My peyne were quyt me rychely.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2600">2600</a></font></span> Allas, to gret a thing aske I!<br> <a name="an_2601"></a> Hit is but foly and wrong wenyng<br> <a name="an_2602"></a> To aske so outrageous a thyng;<br> <a name="an_2603"></a> And whoso askith folily,<br> <a name="an_2604"></a> He mot be warned hastily.<br> <a name="an_2605"></a> And I ne wot what I may say,<br> <a name="an_2606"></a> I am so fer out of the way;<br> <a name="an_2607"></a> For I wolde have full gret likyng<br> <a name="an_2608"></a> And full gret joye of lasse thing.<br> <a name="an_2609"></a> For wolde she, of hir gentylnesse,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2610">2610</a></font></span> Without and more, me oonys kysse,<br> <a name="an_2611"></a> It were to me a gret guerdoun,<br> <a name="an_2612"></a> Relees of all my passioun.<br> <a name="an_2613"></a> But it is hard to come therto;<br> <a name="an_2614"></a> All is but folye that I do,<br> <a name="an_2615"></a> So high I have myn herte set,<br> <a name="an_2616"></a> Where I may no comfort get.<br> <a name="an_2617"></a> I wote not wher I seye well or nought,<br> <a name="an_2618"></a> But this I wot wel in my thought,<br> <a name="an_2619"></a> That it were better of hir alloone,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2620">2620</a></font></span> For to stynte my woo and name="an_2624"></a> A, Lord! Wher I shall byde the day<br> <a name="an_2625"></a> That evere she shall my lady be?<br> <a name="an_2626"></a> He is full cured that may hir see.<br> <a name="an_2627"></a> A, God! Whanne shal the dawnyng spring?<br> <a name="an_2628"></a> To liggen thus is an angry thyng;<br> <a name="an_2629"></a> I have no joye thus heere to ly,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" in ese.<br> <a name="an_2633"></a> I wolde it dawed, and were now day,<br> <a name="an_2634"></a> And that the nyght were went away;<br> <a name="an_2635"></a> For were it day, I wolde uprise.<br> <a name="an_2636"></a> A, slowe sonne, shewe thin enprise!<br> <a name="an_2637"></a> Sped thee to sprede thy beemys bright,<br> <a name="an_2638"></a> And chace the derknesse of the nyght,<br> <a name="an_2647"></a> Out of thy bedde, and harneyse thee,<br> <a name="an_2648"></a> Er evere dawnyng thou maist see.<br> <a name="an_2649"></a> All pryvyly thanne shalt thou goon,<br> <span name="an_2652"></a> Thider she dwellith that is so swet,<br> <a name="an_2653"></a> The which may fall a-slepe be,<br> <a name="an_2654"></a> And thenkith but lytel upon thee.<br> <a name="an_2683"></a> Makith lovers, withouten ony wene,<br> <a name="an_2684"></a> Under her clothes pale and lene.<br> <a name="an_2685"></a> For Love leveth colour ne cleernesse;<br> <a name="an_2686"></a> Who loveth trewe hath no fatnesse.<br> <a name="an_2687"></a> Thou shalt wel by thysilf see<br> <a name="an_2688"></a> That thou must nedis assayed be.<br> <a name="an_2691"></a> It is no wonder though they be fatt;<br> <a name="an_2692"></a> With false othes her loves they gatt.<br> <a name="an_2693"></a> For oft I see suche losengours<br> <a name="an_2694"></a> Fatter than abbatis or priours.<br> <a name="an_2695"></a> "Yit with o thing I thee charge,<br> <a name="an_2696"></a> That is to seye, that thou be large<br> <a name="an_2721"></a> Whanne Love all this hadde boden me,<br> <a name="an_2722"></a> I seide hym: "Sire, how may it be<br> <a name="an_2723"></a> That lovers may in such manere<br> <a name="an_2724"></a> Endure the peyne ye have seid heere?<br> <a name="an_2725"></a> I merveyle me wonder faste<br> <a name="an_2726"></a> How ony man may lyve or laste<br> <a name="an_2727"></a> In such peyne and such brennyng,<br> <a name="an_2728"></a> In sorwe and thought and such sighing,<br> <a name="an_2729"></a> Ay unrelesed woo to make,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" I<br> <a name="an_2733"></a> How man, but he were maad of stele,<br> <a name="an_2734"></a> Myght lyve a month, such peynes to fele."<br> <a name="an_2735"></a> The God of Love thanne seide me:<br> <a name="an_2736"></a> "Freend, by the feith I owe to thee,<br> <a name="an_2737"></a> May no man have good, but he it by.<br> <a name="an_2738"></a> A man loveth more tendirly<br> <a <a name="an_2741"></a> In thank that thyng is taken more,<br> <a name="an_2742"></a> For which a man hath suffred sore.<br> <a name="an_2743"></a> Certis, no wo ne may atteyne<br> <a dropes that of the water be.<br> <a name="an_2748"></a> For drye as well the greete see<br> <a name="an_2749"></a> Thou myghtist as the harmes telle<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2750">2750</a></font></span> Of hem that with love dwelle<br> <a name="an_2751"></a> In servyse, for peyne hem sleeth.<br> <a name="an_2752"></a> And yet ech man wolde fle the deeth,<br> <a name="an_2753"></a> And trowe thei shulde nevere escape,<br> <a name="an_2754"></a> Nere that hope couth. hem make<br> <a name="an_2755"></a> Glad, as man in prisoun sett,<br> <a name="an_2756"></a> And may not geten for to et<br> <a name="an_2757"></a> But barly breed and watir pure,<br> <a name="an_2758"></a> And lyeth in vermyn and in ordure;<br> <a name="an_2759"></a> With maketh wene that he shall be<br> <a name="an_2762"></a> Delyvered, and come to liberte.<br> <a name="an_2763"></a> In fortune is [his] fulle trust,<br> <a name="an_2764"></a> Though he lye in strawe name="an_2781"></a> Good hope is curteis for to please,<br> <a name="an_2782"></a> To kepe lovers from all disese.<br> <a name="an_2783"></a> Hope kepith his bond, and wole abide,<br> <a name="an_2787"></a> Hope is her helpe whanne myster is.<br> <a name="an_2788"></a> "And I shall yeve thee eke, iwys,<br> <a name="an_2789"></a> Three other thingis that gret solas<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2790">2790</a></font></span> Doth to hem that be in my las.<br> <a name="an_2791"></a> The firste good that may be founde<br> <a name="an_2795"></a> Best in thyn herte, where she be --<br> <a name="an_2796"></a> Thenkyng in absence is good to thee.<br> <a name="an_2797"></a> Whanne ony lover doth compleyne,<br> <a name="an_2800">2800</a></font></span> Awey his angre for to dryve:<br> <a name="an_2801"></a> It makith lovers to have remembraunce<br> <a name="an_2802"></a> Of comfort and of high plesaunce<br> <a name="an_2803"></a> That Hope hath hight hym for to wynne.<br> <a name="an_2804"></a> For Thought anoon thanne shall bygynne,<br> <a name="an_2805"></a> As fer, God wot, as he can fynde,<br> <a name="an_2806"></a> To make a mirrour of his mynde;<br> <a name="an_2807"></a> For to biholde he wole not lette.<br> <a name="an_2808"></a> Hir persone he shall afore hym sette,<br> <a name="an_2809"></a> Hir laughing eyen, persaunt and clere,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2810">2810</a></font></span> Hir shape, hir forme, hir goodly chere,<br> <a name="an_2811"></a> Hir mouth, that is so gracious,<br> <a name="an_2812"></a> So swete and eke so saverous;<br> <a name="an_2813"></a> Of all hir fetures he shall take heede,<br> <a name="an_2825"></a> "The secounde shal be Swete-Speche,<br> <a name="an_2826"></a> That hath to many oon be leche,<br> <a name="an_2827"></a> To bringe hem out of woo and wer,<br> <a name="an_2828"></a> And holpe many a bachiler,<br> <a name="an_2829"></a> And many a lady sent socour,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2830">2830</a></font></span> That have loved paramour,<br> <a name="an_2831"></a> Thorough spekyng, whanne they myghte heere<br> <a name="an_2832"></a> Of her lovers to hem so dere.<br> <a name="an_2833"></a> To hem it voidith all her smerte,<br> <a name="an_2834"></a> The which is closed in her herte.<br> <a name="an_2835"></a> In herte it makith hem glad and light,<br> <a name="an_2836"></a> Speche, whanne they [ne] mowe have sight.<br> <a name="an_2837"></a> And therfore now it cometh to mynde,<br> <a name="an_2838"></a> In olde dawes, as I fynde,<br> <a name="an_2839"></a> That clerkis writen that hir knewe,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2840">2840</a></font></span> Ther was a lady fresh of hewe,<br> <a name="an_2841"></a> Which of hir love made a song<br> <a name="an_2842"></a> On hym for to remembre among,<br> <a name="an_2843"></a> In which she seyde, `Whanne that I here<br> <a name="an_2844"></a> Speken of hym that is so dere,<br> <a name="an_2845"></a> To me it voidith all smert,<br> <a name="an_2846"></a> Iwys, he sittith so ner myn hert.<br> <a name="an_2847"></a> To speke of hym, at eve or morwe,<br> <a name="an_2848"></a> It cureth me of all my sorwe.<br> <a name="an_2849"></a> To me is noon so high plesaunce<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_2850">2850</a></font></span> As of his persone dalyaunce.'<br> <a name="an_2851"></a> She wist full well that Swete-Spekyng<br> <a name="an_2852"></a> Comfortith in full myche thyng.<br> <a name="an_2853"></a> Hir love she hadde full well assayed;<br> <a name="an_2854"></a> Of him she was full well apaied;<br> <a name="an_2855"></a> To speke of hym hir joye was sett.<br> <a name="an_2856"></a> Therfore I rede thee that thou gett<br> <a name="an_2857"></a> A felowe that can well concele,<br> <a name="an_2858"></a> And kepe thi counsell, and well hele,<br> <a name="an_2861"></a> To gete comfort to hym thou goo,<br> <a name="an_2862"></a> And pryvyly, bitwene yow twoo,<br> <a name="an_2863"></a> Yee shall speke of that goodly thyng<br> <a name="an_2872"></a> Bothe of thi wele and of thi woo.<br> <a name="an_2873"></a> And if his herte to love be sett,<br> <a name="an_2874"></a> His companye is myche the bett,<br> <a name="an_3107"></a> In me fyve woundes dide he make,<br> <a name="an_3108"></a> The soore of whiche shall nevere slake,<br> <a name="an_3109"></a> But ye the botoun graunte me,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3110">3110</a></font></span> Which is moost passaunt of beaute,<br> <a name="an_3111"></a> My lyf, my deth, and my martire,<br> <a name="an_3112"></a> And tresour that I moost desire."<br> <a name="an_3113"></a> Thanne Bialacoil, affrayed all,<br> <a name="an_3114"></a> Seyde, "Sir, it may not fall;<br> <a name="an_3115"></a> That ye desire, it may not arise.<br> <a name="an_3116"></a> What? Wolde ye shende me in this wise?<br> <a name="an_3117"></a> A mochel fool thanne I were,<br> <a name="an_3118"></a> If I suffride you awey to bere<br> <a name="an_3119"></a> The fresh botoun so faire of sight.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3120">3120</a></font></span> For it were neither skile ne right,<br> <a name="an_3121"></a> Of the roser ye broke the rynde,<br> <a name="an_3122"></a> Or take the Rose aforn his kynde.<br> <a name="an_3123"></a> Ye are not curteys to aske it.<br> <a name="an_3124"></a> Late it still on the roser sitt<br> <a name="an_3125"></a> And growe til it amended be,<br> <a name="an_3126"></a> And parfytly come to beaute.<br> <a name="an_3127"></a> I nolde not that it pulled were<br> <a name="an_3128"></a> Fro the roser that it bere,<br> <a name="an_3129"></a> To me it is so leef and deer."<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3130">3130</a></font></span> With that sterte oute anoon Daunger,<br> <a name="an_3131"></a> Out of the place were he was hid.<br> <a name="an_3132"></a> His malice in his chere was kid;<br> <a name="an_3133"></a> Full gret he was and blak of hewe,<br> <a name="an_3134"></a> Sturdy and hidous, whoso hym knewe;<br> <a name="an_3135"></a> Like sharp urchouns his her was growe;<br> <a name="an_3137"></a> His nose frounced, full kirked stood.<br> <a name="an_3138"></a> He com criand as he were wood,<br> <a name="an_3139"></a> And seide, "Bialacoil, telle me why<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3143"></a> He thenkith to dishonoure thee;<br> <a name="an_3144"></a> Thou art wel worthy to have maugree<br> <a name="an_3145"></a> To late hym of the roser wit.<br> <a name="an_3146"></a> Who serveth a feloun is yvel quit.<br> <a name="an_3147"></a> Thou woldist have doon gret bounte,<br> <a name="an_3148"></a> And he with shame wolde quyte thee.<br> <a name="an_3149"></a> Fle hennes, felowe! I rede thee goo!<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3150">3150</a></font></span> It wanteth litel I wole thee sloo.<br> <a name="an_3151"></a> For Bialacoil ne knew thee nought,<br> <a name="an_3152"></a> Whanne thee to serve he sette his thought;<br> <a name="an_3153"></a> For thou wolt shame hym, if thou myght,<br> <a name="an_3154"></a> Bothe ageyns resoun and right.<br> <a name="an_3155"></a> I wole no more in thee affye,<br> <a name="an_3156"></a> That comest so slyghly for t' espye;<br> <a name="an_3157"></a> For it preveth wonder well,<br> <a name="an_3158"></a> Thy slight and tresoun, every deell."<br> <a name="an_3159"></a> I durst no more there make abod<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3160">3160</a></font></span> For the cherl, he was so wod,<br> <a name="an_3161"></a> So gan he threte and manace,<br> <a name="an_3162"></a> And thurgh the haye he dide me chace.<br> <a name="an_3163"></a> For feer of hym I tremblyde and quok,<br> <a name="an_3164"></a> So cherlishly his heed it shok,<br> <a name="an_3165"></a> And seide, if eft he myght me take,<br> <a name="an_3166"></a> I shulde not from his hondis scape.<br> <a name="an_3167"></a> Thanne Bialacoil is fled and mat,<br> <a name="an_3168"></a> And I, all sool, disconsolat,<br> <a name="an_3169"></a> Was left aloone in peyne and thought;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3170">3170</a></font></span> For shame to deth I was nygh brought.<br> <a name="an_3171"></a> Thanne thought I on myn high foly,<br> <a name="an_3172"></a> How that my body utterly<br> <a name="an_3173"></a> Was yeve to peyne and to martire;<br> <a name="an_3174"></a> And therto hadde I so gret ire,<br> <a name="an_3175"></a> That I ne durst the hayes passe.<br> <a name="an_3176"></a> There was noon hope; there was no grace.<br> <a name="an_3177"></a> I trowe nevere man wiste of peyne,<br> <a name="an_3178"></a> But he were laced in loves cheyne;<br> <a name="an_3179"></a> Ne no man [wot], and sooth it is,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3180">3180</a></font></span> But if he love, what anger is.<br> <a name="an_3181"></a> Love holdith his heest to me right wel,<br> <a name="an_3182"></a> Whanne peyne he seide I shulde fel;<br> <a name="an_3183"></a> Noon herte may thenke, ne tunge seyn,<br> <a name="an_3184"></a> A quarter of my woo and peyn.<br> <a name="an_3185"></a> I myght not with the anger laste;<br> <a name="an_3186"></a> Myn herte in poynt was for to braste,<br> <a name="an_3187"></a> Whanne I thought on the Rose, that soo<br> <a name="an_3188"></a> Was thurgh Daunger cast me froo.<br> <a name="an_3189"></a> A long while stod I in that stat,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3190">3190</a></font></span> Til that me saugh so mad and mat<br> <a name="an_3191"></a> The lady of the highe ward,<br> <a name="an_3192"></a> Which from hir tour lokide thiderward.<br> <a name="an_3193"></a> Resoun men clepe that lady,<br> <a name="an_3194"></a> Which from hir tour delyverly<br> <a name="an_3195"></a> Com doun to me, withouten mor.<br> <a name="an_3196"></a> But she was neither yong ne hoor,<br> <a name="an_3197"></a> Ne high ne lowe, ne fat ne lene,<br> <a name="an_3198"></a> But best as it were in a mene.<br> <a name="an_3199"></a> Hir eyen twoo were cleer and light<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" persoune,<br> <a name="an_3203"></a> For round enviroun, hir crownet<br> <a name="an_3204"></a> Was full of riche stonys frett.<br> <a name="an_3205"></a> Hir goodly semblaunt, by devys,<br> <a <a name="an_3218"></a> Resoun bigan to me hir tale.<br> <a name="an_3219"></a> She seide, "Al hayl, my swete freend!<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a May,<br> <a name="an_3223"></a> That made thyn herte mery to be.<br> <a name="an_3224"></a> In yvell tyme thou wentist to see<br> <a name="an_3225"></a> The gardyn, whereof Ydilnesse<br> <a name="an_3231"></a> She hath [thee] trasshed, withoute wen.<br> <a name="an_3232"></a> The God of Love hadde the not sen,<br> <a name="an_3233"></a> Ne hadde Ydilnesse thee conveyed<br> <a name="an_3234"></a> In the verger where Myrthe hym pleyed.<br> <a name="an_3235"></a> If foly have supprised thee,<br> <a name="an_3236"></a> Do so that it recovered be,<br> <a name="an_3237"></a> And ywis;<br> <a name="an_3266"></a> Wherfore to thee bettir is<br> <a name="an_3267"></a> From these folk awey to fare,<br> <a name="an_3268"></a> For they wole make thee lyve in care.<br> <a <a name="an_3289"></a> Of God of Love to hastily;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3290">3290</a></font></span> Ther was no wisdom, but foly.<br> <a <a name="an_3305"></a> Whanne I hir herd thus me chastise,<br> <a name="an_3306"></a> I answerd in ful angry wise.<br> <a name="an_3307"></a> I prayed hir ceessen of hir speche,<br> <a name="an_3351"></a> I tolde hym all, withoute wer,<br> <a name="an_3352"></a> And made my compleynt on Daunger,<br> <a name="an_3353"></a> How for to see he was hidous,<br> <a name="an_3354"></a> And Daunger,<br> <a name="an_3372"></a> And how he is feers of his cheer,<br> <a name="an_3373"></a> At prime temps, love to manace;<br> <a name="an_3374"></a> Ful ofte I have ben in his caas.<br> <a <a name="an_3383"></a> Of herte pray hym specialy<br> <a name="an_3384"></a> Of thy trespas to have mercy,<br> <a name="an_3385"></a> And hote hym wel, here to plese,<br> <a name="an_3386"></a> That seid to me so wel<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3390">3390</a></font></span> That he me esid hath somdell,<br> <a name="an_3391"></a> And eke allegged of my name="an_3395"></a> To Daunger came I all ashamed,<br> <a name="an_3396"></a> The which aforn me hadde blamed,<br> <a name="an_3397"></a> Desiryng for to pese my woo,<br> <a name="an_3398"></a> But over hegge durst I not goo,<br> <a name="an_3399"></a> For he forbed me the passage.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3400">3400</a></font></span> I fond hym cruel in his rage,<br> <a name="an_3401"></a> And in his hond a gret burdoun.<br> <a name="an_3402"></a> To hym I knelide lowe adoun,<br> <a name="an_3403"></a> Ful meke of port and symple of chere,<br> <a name="an_3404"></a> And seide, "Sir, I am comen heere<br> <a name="an_3405"></a> Oonly to aske of you mercy.<br> <a name="an_3406"></a> That greveth me full gretly<br> <a name="an_3407"></a> That trespassed hidirto,<br> <a name="an_3413"></a> Fro whom I ne may withdrawe myn hert.<br> <a name="an_3414"></a> Yit shall [I] never, for joy ne smert,<br> <a name="an_3415"></a> What so bifalle, good what recchith me,<br> <a name="an_3448"></a> So [thou] fer fro my roses be?<br> <a name="an_3449"></a> Trust not on me, for noon assay,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a <a name="an_3453"></a> Unto my freend, and tolde hym all,<br> <a name="an_3454"></a> Which was right joyful of my tall.<br> <a name="an_3455"></a> He seide, "Now goth wel thyn affaire.<br> <a name="an_3671"></a> Agayn her dar I nat mysdo,<br> <a name="an_3672"></a> For alway byddeth she me so<br> <a name="an_3673"></a> To yeve no lover leave to kys,<br> <a name="an_3674"></a> For who attayne<br> <a name="an_3678"></a> Of loves payne hath (soth to sayne)<br> <a name="an_3679"></a> The beste and most avenaunt,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3680">3680</a></font></span> And ernest of the remenaunt."<br> <a name="an_3681"></a> Of his answere I sighed sore;<br> <a name="an_3682"></a> I durst assaye him tho no more,<br> <a name="an_3683"></a> I hadde such drede to greve him ay.<br> <a name="an_3684"></a> A man shulde nat to moche assay<br> <a name="an_3685"></a> To chafe hys frend out of measure,<br> <a longe<br> <a name="an_3695"></a> Aftir the kis, in peyne and woo,<br> <a name="an_3696"></a> Sith I to kis desired soo;<br> <a name="an_3697"></a> Till that, rewyng on my distresse,<br> <a good entaile,<br> <a name="an_3712"></a> Right wondirfull of apparayle.<br> <a name="an_3713"></a> Bi hir atyr so bright and shen<br> <a name="an_3714"></a> Men myght perceyve well and sen<br> <a name="an_3715"></a> She was not of religioun.<br> <a name="an_3716"></a> Nor I nell make mencioun<br> <a name="an_3717"></a> Nor of robe, nor of tresour,<br> <a name="an_3718"></a> Of broche, neithir <a name="an_3745"></a> Oonly to pleyen and to kisse.<br> <a name="an_3746"></a> Graunte hym a kis, of gentilnysse!<br> <a name="an_3747"></a> His teth arn also white and clene;<br> <a name="an_3748"></a> Me thinkith wrong, withouten wene,<br> <a name="an_3749"></a> If ye now werne hym, trustith me,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3954"></a> And with her trowandyse to blende.<br> <a name="an_3955"></a> A fool is eythe to bigyle;<br> <a name="an_3956"></a> But may I lyve a litel while,<br> <a name="an_3957"></a> He shal forthenke his fair semblaunt."<br> <a name="an_3958"></a> And with that word came Drede avaunt,<br> <a name="an_3959"></a> Which was abasshed and in gret fere,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3960">3960</a></font></span> Whanne he wiste Jelousie was there.<br> <a name="an_3961"></a> He was for drede in sich affray<br> <a name="an_3962"></a> That not a word durste he say,<br> <a name="an_3963"></a> But quakyng stod full still aloon,<br> <a name="an_3964"></a> Til Jelousie his weye was gon,<br> <a name="an_3965"></a> Save Shame, that him not forsok.<br> <a name="an_3966"></a> Bothe Drede and she ful sore quok,<br> <a name="an_3967"></a> That atte laste Drede abreyde,<br> <a name="an_3968"></a> And to his cosyn Shame seide:<br> <a name="an_3969"></a> "Shame," he seide, "in sothfastnesse,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3970">3970</a></font></span> To me it is gret hevynesse<br> <a name="an_3971"></a> That the noyse so fer is go,<br> <a name="an_3972"></a> And the sclaundre of us twoo.<br> <a name="an_3973"></a> But sithe that it is byfalle,<br> <a name="an_3974"></a> We may it not ageyn calle<br> <a name="an_3975"></a> Whanne onys sprongen is a fame.<br> <a name="an_3976"></a> For many a yeer withouten blame<br> <a name="an_3977"></a> We han ben, and many a day;<br> <a name="an_3978"></a> For many an Aprill and many a May<br> <a name="an_3979"></a> We han passed, not shamed,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3980">3980</a></font></span> Till Jelousie hath us blamed,<br> <a name="an_3981"></a> Of mystrust and suspecioun,<br> <a name="an_3982"></a> Causeles, withoute enchesoun.<br> <a name="an_3983"></a> Go we to Daunger hastily,<br> <a name="an_3984"></a> And late us shewe hym openly<br> <a name="an_3985"></a> That [he] hath not aright wrought,<br> <a name="an_3986"></a> Whanne that [he] sette nought his thought<br> <a name="an_3987"></a> To kepe better the purprise;<br> <a name="an_3988"></a> In his doyng he is not wise.<br> <a name="an_3989"></a> He hath to us do gret wrong,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_3990">3990</a></font></span> That hath suffred now so long<br> <a name="an_3991"></a> Bialacoil to have his wille,<br> <a name="an_3992"></a> All his lustes to fulfille.<br> <a name="an_3993"></a> He must amende it utterly,<br> <a name="an_3994"></a> Or ellys shall he vilaynesly<br> <a name="an_3995"></a> Exiled be out of this lond;<br> <a name="an_3996"></a> For he the werre may not withstond<br> <a name="an_3997"></a> Of Jelousie, nor the greef,<br> <a name="an_3998"></a> Sith Bialacoil is at myscheef."<br> <a name="an_3999"></a> To Daunger, Shame and Drede anoon<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4000">4000</a></font></span> The righte weye ben goon.<br> <a name="an_4001"></a> The cherl thei founden hem aforn,<br> <a name="an_4002"></a> Liggyng undir an hawethorn;<br> <a name="an_4003"></a> Undir his heed no pilowe was,<br> <a name="an_4004"></a> But in the stede a trusse of gras.<br> <a name="an_4005"></a> He slombred, and a nappe he tok,<br> <a name="an_4006"></a> Tyll Shame pitously hym shok,<br> <a name="an_4007"></a> And grete manace on hym gan make.<br> <a name="an_4008"></a> "Why slepist thou, whanne thou shulde wake?"<br> <a name="an_4009"></a> Quod Shame; "Thou doist us vylanye!<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4010">4010</a></font></span> Who tristith thee, he doth folye,<br> <a name="an_4011"></a> To kepe roses or botouns,<br> <a name="an_4012"></a> Whanne thei ben faire in her sesouns.<br> <a name="an_4013"></a> Thou art woxe to familiere,<br> <a name="an_4014"></a> Where thou shulde be straunge of chere,<br> <a name="an_4015"></a> Stout of thi port, redy to greve.<br> <a name="an_4016"></a> Thou doist gret folye for to leve<br> <a name="an_4017"></a> Bialacoil hereinne to calle<br> <a name="an_4018"></a> The yonder man to shenden us alle.<br> <a name="an_4019"></a> Though that thou slepe, we may here<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4020">4020</a></font></span> Of Jelousie gret noyse heere.<br> <a name="an_4021"></a> Art thou now late? Ris up in hy,<br> <a name="an_4022"></a> And stop sone and delyverly<br> <a name="an_4023"></a> All the gappis of the haye.<br> <a name="an_4024"></a> Do no favour, I thee praye.<br> <a name="an_4025"></a> It fallith nothyng to thy name<br> <a name="an_4026"></a> To make faire semblaunt, where thou maist blame.<br> <a name="an_4027"></a> Yf Bialacoil be sweete and free,<br> <a name="an_4028"></a> Dogged and fell thou shuldist be,<br> <a name="an_4029"></a> Froward and outrageous, ywis;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4030">4030</a></font></span> A cherl chaungeth that curteis is.<br> <a name="an_4031"></a> This have I herd ofte in seiyng,<br> <a name="an_4032"></a> That man [ne] may, for no dauntyng,<br> <a name="an_4033"></a> Make a sperhauk of a bosard.<br> <a name="an_4034"></a> Alle men wole holde thee for musard,<br> <a name="an_4035"></a> That debonair have founden thee;<br> <a name="an_4036"></a> It sittith thee nought curteis to be.<br> <a name="an_4037"></a> To do men plesaunce or servise,<br> <a name="an_4038"></a> In thee it is recreaundise.<br> <a name="an_4039"></a> Let thi werkis fer and ner<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4040">4040</a></font></span> Be like thi name, which is Daunger."<br> <a name="an_4041"></a> Thanne, all abawid in shewing,<br> <a name="an_4042"></a> Anoon spak Drede, right thus seiyng,<br> <a name="an_4043"></a> And seide, "Daunger, I drede me<br> <a name="an_4044"></a> That thou ne wolt bisy be<br> <a name="an_4045"></a> To kepe that thou hast to kepe:<br> <a name="an_4046"></a> Whanne thou shuldist wake, thou art aslepe.<br> <a name="an_4047"></a> Thou shalt be greved, certeynly,<br> <a name="an_4048"></a> If the aspie Jelousy,<br> <a name="an_4049"></a> Or if he fynde thee in blame.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4050">4050</a></font></span> He hath to-day assailed Shame,<br> <a name="an_4051"></a> And chased awey with gret manace<br> <a name="an_4052"></a> Bialacoil out of this place,<br> <a name="an_4053"></a> And swereth shortly that he shall<br> <a name="an_4054"></a> Enclose hym in a sturdy wall;<br> <a name="an_4055"></a> And all is for thi wikkednesse,<br> <a name="an_4056"></a> For that thee faileth straungenesse.<br> <a name="an_4057"></a> Thyn herte, I trowe, be failed all;<br> <a name="an_4058"></a> Thou shalt repente in speciall,<br> <a name="an_4059"></a> If Jelousie the soothe knewe;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4060">4060</a></font></span> Thou shalt forthenke and sore rewe."<br> <a name="an_4061"></a> With that the cherl his clubbe gan shake,<br> <a name="an_4062"></a> Frounyng his eyen gan to make,<br> <a name="an_4063"></a> And hidous chere; as man in rage<br> <a name="an_4064"></a> For ire he brente in his visage,<br> <a name="an_4065"></a> Whanne that [he] herd hym blamed soo.<br> <a name="an_4066"></a> He seide, "Out of my wit I goo!<br> <a name="an_4067"></a> To be discomfyt I have gret wrong.<br> <a name="an_4068"></a> Certis, I have now lyved to long,<br> <a name="an_4069"></a> Sith I may not this closer kepe.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4070">4070</a></font></span> All quyk I wolde be dolven deepe,<br> <a name="an_4071"></a> If ony man shal more repeire<br> <a name="an_4072"></a> Into this gardyn, for foule or faire.<br> <a name="an_4073"></a> Myn herte for ire goth a-fere,<br> <a name="an_4074"></a> That I let ony entre heere.<br> <a name="an_4075"></a> I have do folie, now I see,<br> <a name="an_4076"></a> But now it shall amended bee.<br> <a name="an_4077"></a> Who settith foot heere ony more,<br> <a name="an_4078"></a> Truly he shall repente it sore;<br> <a name="an_4079"></a> For no man moo into this place<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4080">4080</a></font></span> Of me to entre shal have grace.<br> <a name="an_4081"></a> Lever I hadde with swerdis tweyne<br> <a name="an_4082"></a> Thurghoute myn herte in every veyne<br> <a name="an_4083"></a> Perced to be with many a wounde,<br> <a name="an_4084"></a> Thanne slouthe shulde in me be founde.<br> <a name="an_4085"></a> From hennes forth, by nyght or day,<br> <a name="an_4086"></a> I shall defende it, if I may,<br> <a name="an_4087"></a> Withouten ony excepcioun<br> <a name="an_4088"></a> Of ech maner condicioun.<br> <a name="an_4089"></a> And if I it eny man graunt,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4090">4090</a></font></span> Holdeth me for recreaunt."<br> <a name="an_4091"></a> Thanne Daunger on his feet gan stond,<br> <a name="an_4092"></a> And hente a burdoun in his hond.<br> <a name="an_4093"></a> Wroth in his ire, ne lefte he nought,<br> <a name="an_4094"></a> But thurgh the verger he hath sought.<br> <a name="an_4095"></a> If he myght fynde hole or trace,<br> <a name="an_4096"></a> Wherethurgh that me mot forth-by pace,<br> <a name="an_4097"></a> Or ony gappe, he dide it close,<br> <a name="an_4098"></a> That no man myghte touche a rose<br> <a name="an_4099"></a> Of the roser all aboute.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4100">4100</a></font></span> He shitteth every man withoute.<br> <a name="an_4101"></a> Thus day by day Daunger is wers,<br> <a name="an_4102"></a> More wondirfull and more dyvers,<br> <a name="an_4103"></a> And feller eke than evere he was.<br> <a name="an_4104"></a> For hym full ofte I synge "Allas!"<br> <a name="an_4105"></a> For I ne may nought, thurgh his ire,<br> <a name="an_4106"></a> Recovere that I moost desire.<br> <a name="an_4107"></a> Myn herte, allas, wole brest a-twoo,<br> <a name="an_4108"></a> For Bialacoil I wratthed soo.<br> <a name="an_4109"></a> For certeynly, in every membre<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4110">4110</a></font></span> I quake, whanne I me remembre<br> <a name="an_4111"></a> Of the botoun, which I wolde<br> <a name="an_4112"></a> Full ofte a day sen and biholde.<br> <a name="an_4113"></a> And whanne I thenke upon the kiss,<br> <a name="an_4114"></a> And how myche joye and bliss<br> <a name="an_4115"></a> I hadde thurgh the savour swete,<br> <a name="an_4116"></a> For want of it I grone and grete.<br> <a name="an_4117"></a> Me thenkith I fele yit in my nose<br> <a name="an_4118"></a> The swete savour of the Rose.<br> <a name="an_4119"></a> And now I woot that I mot goo<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4120">4120</a></font></span> So fer the freshe floures froo,<br> <a name="an_4121"></a> To me full welcome were the deth.<br> <a name="an_4122"></a> Absens therof, allas, me sleeth.<br> <a name="an_4123"></a> For whilom with this Rose -- allas! --<br> <a name="an_4124"></a> I touched nose, mouth, and face;<br> <a name="an_4125"></a> But now the deth I must abide.<br> <a name="an_4126"></a> But Love consente another tyde<br> <a name="an_4127"></a> That onys I touche may and kisse,<br> <a name="an_4128"></a> I trowe my peyne shall never lisse;<br> <a name="an_4129"></a> Theron is all my coveitise,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4130">4130</a></font></span> Which brent myn herte in many wise.<br> <a name="an_4131"></a> Now shal repaire agayn sighinge,<br> <a name="an_4132"></a> Long wacche on nyghtis, and no slepinge,<br> <a name="an_4133"></a> Thought in wisshing, torment and woo,<br> <a name="an_4134"></a> With many a turnyng to and froo,<br> <a name="an_4135"></a> That half my peyne I can not telle.<br> <a name="an_4136"></a> For I am fallen into helle<br> <a name="an_4137"></a> From paradys, and wel the more<br> <a name="an_4138"></a> My turment greveth. more and more<br> <a name="an_4139"></a> Anoieth now the bittirnesse,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4140">4140</a></font></span> That I toforn have felt swetnesse.<br> <a name="an_4141"></a> And Wikkid-Tunge, thurgh his falshede,<br> <a name="an_4142"></a> Causeth all my woo and drede.<br> <a name="an_4143"></a> On me he leieth a pitous charge,<br> <a name="an_4144"></a> Bicause his tunge was to large.<br> <a name="an_4145"></a> Now it is tyme, shortly, that I<br> <a name="an_4146"></a> Telle you som thyng of Jelousy,<br> <a name="an_4147"></a> That was in gret suspecioun.<br> <a name="an_4148"></a> Aboute hym lefte he no masoun,<br> <a name="an_4149"></a> That stoon coude leye, ne querrour;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4150">4150</a></font></span> He hirede hem to make a tour.<br> <a name="an_4151"></a> And first, the roses for to kep,<br> <a name="an_4152"></a> Aboute hem made he a diche deep,<br> <a name="an_4153"></a> Right wondir large, and also brood;<br> <a name="an_4154"></a> Upon the whiche also stod<br> <a name="an_4155"></a> Of squared stoon a sturdy wall,<br> <a name="an_4156"></a> Which on a cragge was founded all;<br> <a name="an_4157"></a> And right gret thikkenesse eke it bar.<br> <a name="an_4158"></a> Aboute, it was founded squar,<br> <a name="an_4159"></a> An hundred fademe on every sid;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4160">4160</a></font></span> It was all liche longe and wid.<br> <a name="an_4161"></a> Lest ony tyme it were assayled,<br> <a name="an_4162"></a> Ful wel aboute it was batayled,<br> <a name="an_4163"></a> And rounde enviroun eke were set<br> <a name="an_4164"></a> Ful many a riche and fair touret.<br> <a name="an_4165"></a> At every corner of this wall<br> <a name="an_4166"></a> Was set a tour full pryncipall;<br> <a name="an_4167"></a> And everich hadde, withoute fable,<br> <a name="an_4168"></a> A porte-colys defensable<br> <a name="an_4169"></a> To kepe of enemyes, and to greve,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4170">4170</a></font></span> That there her force wolde preve.<br> <a name="an_4171"></a> And eke amydde this purprise<br> <a name="an_4172"></a> Was maad a tour of gret maistrise;<br> <a name="an_4173"></a> A fairer saugh no man with sight,<br> <a name="an_4174"></a> Large and wid, and of gret myght.<br> <a name="an_4175"></a> They dredde noon assaut<br> <a name="an_4176"></a> Of gyn, gunne, nor skaffaut.<br> <a name="an_4177"></a> The temperure of the morter<br> <a name="an_4178"></a> Was maad of lycour wonder der,<br> <a name="an_4179"></a> Of quykke lym, persant and egre,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4180">4180</a></font></span> The which was tempred with vynegre.<br> <a name="an_4181"></a> The stoon was hard, of ademant,<br> <a name="an_4182"></a> Wherof they made the foundement.<br> <a name="an_4183"></a> The tour was round, maad in compas;<br> <a name="an_4184"></a> In all this world no riccher was,<br> <a name="an_4185"></a> Ne better ordeigned therwithall.<br> <a name="an_4186"></a> Aboute the tour was maad a wall,<br> <a name="an_4187"></a> So that bitwixt that and the tour<br> <a name="an_4188"></a> Rosers were sette of swete savour,<br> <a name="an_4189"></a> With many roses that thei bere;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4190">4190</a></font></span> And eke withynne the castell were<br> <a name="an_4191"></a> Spryngoldes, gunnes, bows, and archers;<br> <a name="an_4192"></a> And eke above, atte corners,<br> <a name="an_4193"></a> Men seyn over the wall stonde<br> <a name="an_4194"></a> Grete engynes, who were nygh honde.<br> <a name="an_4195"></a> And in the kernels, heere and there,<br> <a name="an_4196"></a> Of arblasters gret plente were;<br> <a name="an_4197"></a> Noon armure myght her strok withstonde;<br> <a name="an_4198"></a> It were foly to prece to honde.<br> <a name="an_4199"></a> Withoute the diche were lystes maad,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4200">4200</a></font></span> With wall batayled large and brad,<br> <a name="an_4201"></a> For men and hors shulde not atteyne<br> <a name="an_4202"></a> To neigh the dyche over the pleyne.<br> <a name="an_4203"></a> Thus Jelousie hath enviroun<br> <a name="an_4204"></a> Set aboute his garnysoun<br> <a name="an_4205"></a> With walles rounde and diche dep,<br> <a name="an_4206"></a> Oonly the roser for to kep.<br> <a name="an_4207"></a> And Daunger, erly and late,<br> <a name="an_4208"></a> The keyes [kepte] of the utter gate,<br> <a name="an_4209"></a> The which openeth toward the eest.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4210">4210</a></font></span> And he hadde with hym atte leest<br> <a name="an_4211"></a> Thritty servauntes, echon by name.<br> <a name="an_4212"></a> That other gate kepte Shame,<br> <a name="an_4213"></a> Which openede, as it was couth,<br> <a name="an_4214"></a> Toward the partie of the south.<br> <a name="an_4215"></a> Sergeauntes assigned were hir to<br> <a name="an_4216"></a> Ful many, hir wille for to doo.<br> <a name="an_4217"></a> Thanne Drede hadde in hir baillie<br> <a name="an_4218"></a> The kepyng of the conestablerye<br> <a name="an_4219"></a> Toward the north, I undirstond,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4220">4220</a></font></span> That openyde upon the lyft hond;<br> <a name="an_4221"></a> The which for nothyng may be sure,<br> <a name="an_4222"></a> But if she do bisy cure,<br> <a name="an_4223"></a> Erly on morowe and also late,<br> <a name="an_4224"></a> Strongly to shette and barre the gate.<br> <a name="an_4225"></a> Of every thing that she may see<br> <a name="an_4226"></a> Drede is aferd, wherso she be;<br> <a name="an_4227"></a> For with a puff of litell wynd<br> <a name="an_4228"></a> Drede is astonyed in hir mynd.<br> <a name="an_4229"></a> Therfore, for stelyng of the Rose,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4230">4230</a></font></span> I rede hir nought the yate unclose.<br> <a name="an_4231"></a> A foulis flight wol make hir flee,<br> <a name="an_4232"></a> And eke a shadowe, if she it see.<br> <a name="an_4233"></a> Thanne Wikked-Tunge, ful of envye,<br> <a name="an_4234"></a> With soudiours of Normandye,<br> <a name="an_4235"></a> As he that causeth all the bate,<br> <a name="an_4236"></a> Was keper of the fourthe gate,<br> <a name="an_4237"></a> And also to the tother three<br> <a name="an_4238"></a> He wente full ofte for to see.<br> <a name="an_4239"></a> Whanne his lot was to wake anyght,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4240">4240</a></font></span> His instrumentis wolde he dight,<br> <a name="an_4241"></a> For to blowe and make sown<br> <a name="an_4242"></a> Ofter thanne he hath enchesoun,<br> <a name="an_4243"></a> And walken oft upon the wall,<br> <a name="an_4244"></a> Corners and wikettis overall<br> <a name="an_4245"></a> Full narwe serchen and espie;<br> <a name="an_4246"></a> Though he nought fond, yit wolde he lye.<br> <a name="an_4247"></a> Discordaunt ever fro armonye,<br> <a name="an_4248"></a> And distoned from melodie,<br> <a name="an_4249"></a> Controve he wolde, and foule fayle,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4250">4250</a></font></span> With hornepipes of Cornewaile.<br> <a name="an_4251"></a> In floytes made he discordaunce,<br> <a name="an_4252"></a> And in his musyk -- with myschaunce! --<br> <a name="an_4253"></a> He wolde seyn, with notes newe,<br> <a name="an_4254"></a> That he fond no womman trewe,<br> <a name="an_4255"></a> Ne that he saugh never in his lyf<br> <a name="an_4256"></a> Unto hir husbonde a trewe wyf,<br> <a name="an_4257"></a> Ne noon so ful of honeste<br> <a name="an_4258"></a> That she nyl laughe and mery be<br> <a name="an_4259"></a> Whanne that she hereth, or may espie,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4260">4260</a></font></span> A man speken of leccherie.<br> <a name="an_4261"></a> Everich of hem hath som vice:<br> <a name="an_4262"></a> Oon is dishonest, another is nyce;<br> <a name="an_4263"></a> If oon be full of vylanye,<br> <a name="an_4264"></a> Another hath a likerous ye;<br> <a name="an_4265"></a> If oon be full of wantonesse,<br> <a name="an_4266"></a> Another is a chideresse.<br> <a name="an_4267"></a> Thus Wikked-Tunge -- God yeve him shame! --<br> <a name="an_4268"></a> Can putt hem everychon in blame,<br> <a name="an_4269"></a> Withoute desert and causeles;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4270">4270</a></font></span> He lieth, though they ben giltles.<br> <a name="an_4271"></a> I have pite to sen the sorwe<br> <a name="an_4272"></a> That waketh bothe eve and morwe,<br> <a name="an_4273"></a> To innocentis doith such grevaunce.<br> <a name="an_4274"></a> I pray God yeve him evel chaunce,<br> <a name="an_4275"></a> That he ever so bisy is<br> <a name="an_4276"></a> Of ony womman to seyn amys!<br> <a name="an_4277"></a> Eke Jelousie God confound,<br> <a name="an_4278"></a> That hath maad a tour so round,<br> <a name="an_4279"></a> And made aboute a garisoun,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4280">4280</a></font></span> To sette Bealacoil in prisoun,<br> <a name="an_4281"></a> The which is shet there in the tour<br> <a name="an_4282"></a> Ful longe to holde there sojour,<br> <a name="an_4283"></a> There for to lyve in penaunce.<br> <a name="an_4284"></a> And for to do hym more grevaunce,<br> <a name="an_4285"></a> Ther hath ordeyned Jelousie<br> <a name="an_4286"></a> An olde vekke, for to espye<br> <a name="an_4287"></a> The maner of his governaunce;<br> <a name="an_4288"></a> The whiche devel in hir enfaunce<br> <a name="an_4289"></a> Hadde lerned of loves art,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4290">4290</a></font></span> And of his pleyes tok hir part;<br> <a name="an_4291"></a> She was expert in his servise.<br> <a name="an_4292"></a> She knew ech wrench and every gise<br> <a name="an_4293"></a> Of love, and every wile;<br> <a name="an_4294"></a> It was [the] harder hir to gile.<br> <a name="an_4295"></a> Of Bealacoil she tok ay hede,<br> <a name="an_4296"></a> That evere he lyveth in woo and drede.<br> <a name="an_4297"></a> He kepte hym koy and eke pryve,<br> <a name="an_4298"></a> Lest in hym she hadde see<br> <a name="an_4299"></a> Ony foly countenaunce,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4300">4300</a></font></span> For she knew all the olde daunce.<br> <a name="an_4301"></a> And aftir this, whanne Jelousie<br> <a name="an_4302"></a> Hadde Bealacoil in his baillie,<br> <a name="an_4303"></a> And shette hym up that was so fre,<br> <a name="an_4304"></a> For seur of hym he wolde be,<br> <a name="an_4305"></a> He trusteth sore in his castell;<br> <a name="an_4306"></a> The stronge werk hym liketh well.<br> <a name="an_4307"></a> He dradde not that no glotouns<br> <a name="an_4308"></a> Shulde stele his roses or botouns.<br> <a name="an_4309"></a> The roses weren assured all,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4310">4310</a></font></span> Defenced with the stronge wall.<br> <a name="an_4311"></a> Now Jelousie full well may be<br> <a name="an_4312"></a> Of drede devoid in liberte,<br> <a name="an_4313"></a> Whether that he slepe or wake,<br> <a name="an_4314"></a> For his roses may noon be take.<br> <a name="an_4315"></a> But I -- allas! -- now morne shall;<br> <a name="an_4316"></a> Bicause I was withoute the wall,<br> <a name="an_4317"></a> Full moche dool and moone I made.<br> <a name="an_4318"></a> Who hadde wist what woo I hadde,<br> <a name="an_4319"></a> I trowe he wolde have had pite.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4320">4320</a></font></span> Love to deere hadde soold to me<br> <a name="an_4321"></a> The good that of his love hadde I.<br> <a name="an_4322"></a> I wende a bought it all queyntly;<br> <a name="an_4323"></a> But now, thurgh doublyng of my peyn,<br> <a name="an_4324"></a> I see he wolde it selle ageyn,<br> <a name="an_4325"></a> And me a newe bargeyn leere,<br> <a name="an_4326"></a> The which all-oute the more is deere,<br> <a name="an_4327"></a> For the solas that I have lorn,<br> <a name="an_4328"></a> Thanne I hadde it never aforn.<br> <a name="an_4329"></a> Certayn, I am ful lik in deed<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4330">4330</a></font></span> To hym that cast in erthe his seed,<br> <a name="an_4331"></a> And hath joie of the newe spryng,<br> <a name="an_4332"></a> Whanne it greneth in the gynnyng,<br> <a name="an_4333"></a> And is also fair and fresh of flour,<br> <a name="an_4334"></a> Lusty to seen, swoote of odour;<br> <a name="an_4335"></a> But er he it in sheves shere,<br> <a name="an_4336"></a> May falle a weder that shal it dere,<br> <a name="an_4337"></a> And make it to fade and falle,<br> <a name="an_4338"></a> The stalke, the greyn, and floures alle,<br> <a name="an_4339"></a> That to the tylyer is fordon<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4340">4340</a></font></span> The hope that he hadde to soon.<br> <a name="an_4341"></a> I drede, certeyn, that so fare I;<br> <a name="an_4342"></a> For hope and travaile sikerly<br> <a name="an_4343"></a> Ben me byraft all with a storm;<br> <a name="an_4344"></a> The flour nyl seeden of my corn.<br> <a name="an_4345"></a> For Love hath so avaunced me,<br> <a name="an_4346"></a> Whanne I bigan my pryvite<br> <a name="an_4347"></a> To Bialacoil all for to tel,<br> <a name="an_4348"></a> Whom I ne fond froward ne fel,<br> <a name="an_4349"></a> But tok a-gree all hool my play.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4350">4350</a></font></span> But Love is of so hard assay,<br> <a name="an_4351"></a> That al at oonys he reved me,<br> <a name="an_4352"></a> Whanne I wende best aboven to have be.<br> <a name="an_4353"></a> It is of Love, as of Fortune,<br> <a name="an_4354"></a> That chaungeth ofte, and nyl contune,<br> <a name="an_4355"></a> Which whilom wol on folk smyle,<br> <a name="an_4356"></a> And glowmbe on hem another while.<br> <a name="an_4357"></a> Now freend, now foo, [thow] shalt hir feel,<br> <a name="an_4358"></a> For [in] a twynklyng turneth hir wheel.<br> <a name="an_4359"></a> She can writhe hir heed awey;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4360">4360</a></font></span> This is the concours of hir pley.<br> <a name="an_4361"></a> She can areise that doth morne,<br> <a name="an_4362"></a> And whirle adown, and overturne<br> <a name="an_4363"></a> Who sittith hyest, but as hir lust.<br> <a name="an_4364"></a> A fool is he that wole hir trust;<br> <a name="an_4365"></a> For it is I that am come down<br> <a name="an_4366"></a> Thurgh change and revolucioun!<br> <a name="an_4367"></a> Sith Bealacoil mot fro me twynne,<br> <a name="an_4368"></a> Shet in the prisoun yond withynne,<br> <a name="an_4369"></a> His absence at myn herte I fele;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4370">4370</a></font></span> For all my
