<a name="an_4374"></a> Love nyl not that I cured be<br> <a name="an_4375"></a> Of the peynes that I endure,<br> <a name="an_4376"></a> Nor of my cruel aventure.<br> <a name="an_4377"></a> A, Bialacoil, myn owne deer!<br> <a name="an_4378"></a> Though thou be now a prisoner,<br> <a name="an_4379"></a> Kep atte leste thyn herte to me<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4380">4380</a></font></span> And suffre not that it daunted be;<br> <a name="an_4381"></a> Ne lat not Jelousie, in his rage,<br> <a name="an_4382"></a> Putten thin herte in no servage.<br> <a name="an_4383"></a> Although he chastice thee withoute<br> <a name="an_4384"></a> And make thy body unto hym loute,<br> <a name="an_4385"></a> Have herte as hard as dyamaunt,<br> <a name="an_4386"></a> Stedefast and nought pliaunt.<br> <a name="an_4387"></a> In prisoun though thi body be,<br> <a name="an_4388"></a> At large kep thyn herte free;<br> <a name="an_4389"></a> A trewe herte wole not plie<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4390">4390</a></font></span> For no manace that it may drye.<br> <a name="an_4391"></a> If Jelousie doth thee payn,<br> <a name="an_4392"></a> Quyte hym his while thus agayn,<br> <a name="an_4393"></a> To venge thee, atte leest in thought,<br> <a name="an_4394"></a> If other way thou maist nought;<br> <a name="an_4395"></a> And in this wise sotilly<br> <a name="an_4396"></a> Worche, and wynne the maistry.<br> <a name="an_4397"></a> But yit I am in gret affray<br> <a name="an_4398"></a> Lest thou do not as I say.<br> <a name="an_4399"></a> I drede thou canst me gret maugre,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4400">4400</a></font></span> That thou enprisoned art for me;<br> <a name="an_4401"></a> But that [is. not for my trespas,<br> <a name="an_4402"></a> For thurgh me never discovred was<br> <a name="an_4403"></a> Yit thyng that oughte be secree.<br> <a name="an_4404"></a> Wel more anoy is in me,<br> <a name="an_4405"></a> Than is in thee, of this myschaunce;<br> <a name="an_4406"></a> For I endure more hard penaunce,<br> <a name="an_4407"></a> Than ony can seyn or thynke,<br> <a name="an_4408"></a> That for the sorwe almost I synke.<br> <a name="an_4409"></a> Whanne I remembre me of my woo,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" drede.<br> <a name="an_4413"></a> Owe I not wel to have distresse,<br> <a name="an_4414"></a> Whanne false, thurgh hir wikkednesse,<br> <a name="an_4415"></a> And traitours, that arn envyous,<br> <a lust, right at her will.<br> <a name="an_4422"></a> I drede they have thee brought thertill.<br> <a name="an_4423"></a> Withoute comfort, thought me sleeth.<br> <a name="an_4424"></a> This game wole brynge me to my deeth.<br> <a name="an_4425"></a> For if youre goode wille I leese,<br> <a name="an_4426"></a> I mot be deed, I may not chese.<br> <a name="an_4427"></a> And if that thou foryete name="an_4433"></a> Allas, in wanhope? Nay, pardee!<br> <a name="an_4434"></a> For I wole never dispeired be.<br> <a name="an_4435"></a> If hope me faile, thanne am I<br> <a name="an_4436"></a> Ungracious and unworthy.<br> <a name="an_4437"></a> In hope I wole comforted be,<br> <a name="an_4438"></a> For Love, whanne he bitaught hir me,<br> <a name="an_4439"></a> Seide that Hope, whereso I goo,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4440">4440</a></font></span> Shulde ay be relees to my woo.<br> <a name="an_4441"></a> But what and she my baalis beete,<br> <a name="an_4442"></a> And be to me curteis and sweete?<br> <a name="an_4443"></a> She is in nothyng full certeyn.<br> <a name="an_4444"></a> Lovers she putt in full gret peyn,<br> <a name="an_4445"></a> And makith hem with woo to deele.<br> <a name="an_4446"></a> Hir faire biheeste disceyveth feele,<br> <a name="an_4447"></a> For she wole byhote, sikirly,<br> <a name="an_4448"></a> And failen aftir outrely.<br> <a name="an_4449"></a> A, that is a full noyous thyng!<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4450">4450</a></font></span> For many a lover, in lovyng,<br> <a name="an_4451"></a> Hangeth upon hir, and trusteth faste,<br> <a name="an_4452"></a> Whiche leese her travel at the laste.<br> <a name="an_4453"></a> Of thyng to comen she woot right nought;<br> <a name="an_4454"></a> Therfore, if it be wysely sought,<br> <a name="an_4455"></a> Hir counseill foly is to take.<br> <a name="an_4456"></a> For many tymes, whanne she wole make<br> <a name="an_4457"></a> A full good silogisme, I dreede<br> <a name="an_4458"></a> That aftirward ther shal in deede<br> <a name="an_4459"></a> Folwe an evell conclusioun.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4460">4460</a></font></span> This put me in confusioun.<br> <a name="an_4461"></a> For many tymes I have it seen,<br> <a name="an_4462"></a> That many have bigyled been<br> <a name="an_4463"></a> For trust that they have set in Hope,<br> <a name="an_4464"></a> Which fell hem aftirward a-slope.<br> <a name="an_4465"></a> But nevertheles, yit gladly she wolde<br> <a name="an_4466"></a> That he, that wole hym with hir holde,<br> <a color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4470">4470</a></font></span> Whanne I hir blamed, I dide foly.<br> <a name="an_4471"></a> But what avayleth hir good wille,<br> <a name="an_4472"></a> Whanne she ne may staunche my stounde ille?<br> <a name="an_4473"></a> That helpith litel that she may doo,<br> <a name="an_4474"></a> Out-take biheest unto my woo.<br> <a name="an_4475"></a> And heeste certeyn, in no wise,<br> <a name="an_4476"></a> Withoute yift, is not to prise.<br> <a name="an_4477"></a> Whanne heest and deede a-sundry varie,<br> <a name="an_4478"></a> They doon a gret contrarie.<br> <a name="an_4479"></a> Thus am I possed up and doun<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4480">4480</a></font></span> With dool, thought, and confusioun;<br> <a name="an_4481"></a> Of my disese ther is no noumbre.<br> <a name="an_4482"></a> Daunger and Shame me encumbre,<br> <a name="an_4483"></a> Drede also, and Jelousie,<br> <a name="an_4484"></a> And Wikked-Tunge, full of envie,<br> <a name="an_4485"></a> Of whiche the sharpe and cruel ire<br> <a name="an_4486"></a> Full ofte me putte in gret martire.<br> <a name="an_4487"></a> They han my joye fully let,<br> <a name="an_4488"></a> Sith Bialacoil they have bishet<br> <a name="an_4489"></a> Fro me in prisoun wikkidly,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4490">4490</a></font></span> Whom I love so entierly<br> <a name="an_4491"></a> That it wole my bane bee<br> <a name="an_4492"></a> But I the sonner may hym see.<br> <a name="an_4493"></a> And yit moreover, wurst of alle,<br> <a name="an_4494"></a> Ther is set to kepe -- foule hir bifalle! --<br> <a name="an_4495"></a> A rympled vekke, fer ronne in age,<br> <a name="an_4496"></a> Frownyng and yelowe in hir visage,<br> <a name="an_4497"></a> Which in awayt lyth day and nyght,<br> <a name="an_4498"></a> That noon of him may have a sight.<br> <a name="an_4499"></a> Now mote my sorwe enforced be.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4500">4500</a></font></span> Full soth it is that Love yaf me<br> <a name="an_4501"></a> Three wonder yiftes of his grace,<br> <a name="an_4502"></a> Whiche I have lorn now in this place,<br> <a name="an_4503"></a> Sith they ne may, withoute drede,<br> <a name="an_4504"></a> Helpen but lytel, who taketh heede.<br> <a name="an_4505"></a> For here availeth no Swete-Thought,<br> <a name="an_4506"></a> And Sweete-Speche helpith right nought.<br> <a name="an_4507"></a> The thridde was called Swete-Lokyng,<br> <a name="an_4508"></a> That now is lorn, without lesyng.<br> <a name="an_4509"></a> Yiftes were faire, but not forthy<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4510">4510</a></font></span> They helpe me but symply,<br> <a name="an_4511"></a> But Bialacoil loosed be,<br> <a name="an_4512"></a> To gon at large and to be free.<br> <a name="an_4513"></a> For hym my lyf lyth all in doute,<br> <a name="an_4514"></a> But if he come the rather oute.<br> <a name="an_4515"></a> Allas, I trowe it wole not ben!<br> <a name="an_4516"></a> For how shuld I evermore hym sen?<br> <a name="an_4517"></a> He may not out, and that is wrong,<br> <a name="an_4518"></a> By cause the tour is so strong.<br> <a name="an_4519"></a> How shulde he out? By whos prowesse,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4520">4520</a></font></span> Out of so strong a forteresse?<br> <a name="an_4521"></a> By me, certeyn, it nyl be doo;<br> <a name="an_4522"></a> God woot, I have no wit therto!<br> <a name="an_4523"></a> But, wel I woot, I was in rage,<br> <a name="an_4524"></a> Whonne I to Love dide homage.<br> <a name="an_4525"></a> Who was in cause, in sothfastnesse,<br> <a name="an_4526"></a> But hirsilf, Dame Idelnesse,<br> <a name="an_4527"></a> Which me conveied, thurgh my praier,<br> <a name="an_4528"></a> To entre into that faire verger.<br> <a name="an_4529"></a> She was to blame me to leve,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4530">4530</a></font></span> The which now doth me soore greve.<br> <a name="an_4531"></a> A foolis word is nought to trowe,<br> <a name="an_4532"></a> Ne worth an appel for to lowe;<br> <a name="an_4533"></a> Men shulde hym snybbe bittirly,<br> <a name="an_4534"></a> At pryme temps of his foly.<br> <a name="an_4535"></a> I was a fool, and she me leeved,<br> <a name="an_4536"></a> Thurgh whom I am right nought releeved.<br> <a name="an_4537"></a> She accomplisshid all my will,<br> <a name="an_4538"></a> That now me greveth wondir ill.<br> <a name="an_4539"></a> Resoun me seide what shulde falle.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4540">4540</a></font></span> A fool mysilf I may well calle,<br> <a name="an_4541"></a> That love asyde I had [nat] leyd,<br> <a name="an_4542"></a> And trowed that Dame Resoun seid.<br> <a name="an_4543"></a> Resoun hadde bothe skile and ryght,<br> <a name="an_4544"></a> Whanne she me blamed, with all hir myght,<br> <a name="an_4545"></a> To medle of love that hath me shent;<br> <a name="an_4546"></a> But certeyn, now I wole repent.<br> <a name="an_4547"></a> And shulde I repente? Nay, parde!<br> <a name="an_4548"></a> A fals traitour thanne shulde I be.<br> <a name="an_4549"></a> The develes engynnes wolde me take,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4550">4550</a></font></span> If I my lord wolde forsake,<br> <a name="an_4551"></a> Or Bialacoil falsly bitraye.<br> <a name="an_4552"></a> Shulde I at myscheef hate hym? Nay,<br> <a name="an_4553"></a> Sith he now, for his curtesie,<br> <a name="an_4554"></a> Is in prisoun of Jelousie.<br> <a name="an_4555"></a> Curtesie certeyn dide he me,<br> <a name="an_4556"></a> So mych that may not yolden be,<br> <a name="an_4557"></a> Whanne he the hay passen me let,<br> <a name="an_4558"></a> To kisse the Rose, faire and swet.<br> <a name="an_4559"></a> Shulde I therfore cunne hym mawgre?<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4560">4560</a></font></span> Nay, certeynly, it shal not be;<br> <a name="an_4561"></a> For Love shal nevere, yif God wille,<br> <a name="an_4562"></a> Here of me, thurgh word or wille,<br> <a name="an_4563"></a> Offence or complaynt, more or lesse,<br> <a name="an_4564"></a> Neither of Hope nor Idilnesse.<br> <a name="an_4565"></a> For certis, it were wrong that I<br> <a name="an_4566"></a> Hated hem for her curtesy.<br> <a name="an_4567"></a> Ther is not ellys but suffre and thynke,<br> <a name="an_4568"></a> And waken whanne I shulde wynke;<br> <a name="an_4569"></a> Abide in hope, til Love, thurgh chaunce,<br> <span class="margnote"><font that swete.<br> <a name="an_4573"></a> Whilom I thenke how Love to me<br> <a name="an_4574"></a> Seide he wolde take att gree<br> <a name="an_4575"></a> My servise, if unpacience<br> <a name="an_4576"></a> [Ne] caused me to don offence.<br> <a name="an_4577"></a> He seide, "In thank I shal it take,<br> <a name="an_4578"></a> And high maister eke thee make,<br> <a name="an_4579"></a> If wikkednesse ne reve it thee;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4580">4580</a></font></span> But sone, I trowe, that shall not be."<br> <a name="an_4581"></a> These were his wordis, by and by;<br> <a name="an_4582"></a> It semede he lovede me trewely.<br> <a name="an_4583"></a> Now is ther not but serve hym wel,<br> <a name="an_4584"></a> If that I thenke his thank to fel.<br> <a name="an_4585"></a> My good, myn harm lyth hool in me.<br> <a name="an_4586"></a> In Love may no defaute be,<br> <a name="an_4587"></a> For trewe Love ne failide never man.<br> <a name="an_4588"></a> Sothly the faute mot nedys than --<br> <a name="an_4589"></a> As God forbede! -- be founde in me;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4590">4590</a></font></span> And how it cometh, I can not see.<br> <a name="an_4591"></a> Now late it goon as it may goo;<br> <a name="an_4592"></a> Whether Love wole socoure me or sloo,<br> <a name="an_4593"></a> He may do hool on me his will.<br> <a name="an_4594"></a> I am so sore bounde hym till,<br> <a name="an_4595"></a> From his servise I may not fleen;<br> <a name="an_4596"></a> For lyf and deth, withouten wen,<br> <a name="an_4597"></a> Is in his hand -- I may not chese --<br> <a name="an_4598"></a> He may me doo bothe wynne and leese.<br> <a name="an_4599"></a> And sith so sore he doth me greve,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4600">4600</a></font></span> Yit, if my lust he wolde acheve,<br> <a name="an_4601"></a> To Bialacoil goodly to be,<br> <a name="an_4602"></a> I yeve no force what felle on me.<br> <a name="an_4603"></a> For though I dye, as I mot nede,<br> <a name="an_4604"></a> I praye Love, of his goodlyhede,<br> <a name="an_4605"></a> To Bialacoil do gentylnesse,<br> <a name="an_4606"></a> For whom I lyve in such distresse<br> <a name="an_4607"></a> That I mot deyen for penaunce.<br> <a name="an_4608"></a> But first, withoute repentaunce,<br> <a name="an_4609"></a> I wole me confesse in good entent,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4610">4610</a></font></span> And make in haste my testament,<br> <a name="an_4611"></a> As lovers doon that feelen name="an_4615"></a> Thus, as I made my passage<br> <a name="an_4616"></a> In compleynt and in cruel rage,<br> <a name="an_4617"></a> And I not where to fynde a leche<br> <a name="an_4618"></a> That Anoon me telle.<br> <a name="an_4632"></a> Hast thou not yit of love thi fille?<br> <a name="an_4633"></a> Art thou not wery of thy servise,<br> <a name="an_4634"></a> That the hath [greved] in sich wise?<br> <a name="an_4635"></a> What joye hast thou in thy lovyng?<br> <a name="an_4636"></a> Is it swete or bitter thing?<br> <a name="an_4637"></a> Canst thou yit chese, lat me see,<br> <a name="an_4638"></a> What best thi socour myghte be?<br> <a name="an_4639"></a> "Thou servest a full noble lord,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4640">4640</a></font></span> That maketh thee thrall for thi reward,<br> <a name="an_4641"></a> Which ay renewith thy turment,<br> <a name="an_4642"></a> With foly so he hath thee blent.<br> <a name="an_4643"></a> Thou fell in myscheef thilke day<br> <a name="an_4644"></a> Whanne thou didist, the sothe to say,<br> <a name="an_4645"></a> Obeysaunce and eke homage.<br> <a name="an_4646"></a> Thou wroughtest nothyng as the sage,<br> <a name="an_4647"></a> Whanne thou bicam his liege man.<br> <a name="an_4648"></a> Thou didist a gret foly than,<br> <a name="an_4649"></a> Thou wistest not what fell therto,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4650">4650</a></font></span> With what lord thou haddist to do.<br> <a name="an_4651"></a> If thou haddist hym wel knowe,<br> <a name="an_4652"></a> Thou haddist nought be brought so lowe;<br> <a name="an_4653"></a> For if thou wistest what it wer,<br> <a name="an_4654"></a> Thou noldist serve hym half a yeer,<br> <a name="an_4655"></a> Not a weke, nor half a day,<br> <a name="an_4656"></a> Ne yit an hour, withoute delay,<br> <a name="an_4657"></a> Ne never han loved paramours,<br> <a name="an_4658"></a> His lordshipp is so full of shours.<br> <a name="an_4659"></a> Knowest hym ought?" Late se."<br> <a name="an_191-ap"></a> 4661 L'amaunt "Of that he seide I shulde be<br> <a name="an_4662"></a> Glad to have sich lord as he,<br> <a name="an_4663"></a> And maister of sich seignorie."<br> <a name="an_4664"></a> Raisoun "Knowist hym no more?" name="an_4801"></a> And rede it over comunely;<br> <a name="an_4802"></a> But to mysilf lewedist am I.<br> <a name="an_4803"></a> But sith ye love discreven so,<br> <a name="an_4804"></a> And lak and preise it, bothe twoo,<br> <a name="an_4805"></a> Defyneth it into this letter,<br> <a name="an_4806"></a> That I may thenke on it the better;<br> <a name="an_4807"></a> For I herde never diffyne it er,<br> <a name="an_4808"></a> And wilfully I wolde it ler."<br> <a name="an_4809"></a> Raisoun "If love be serched wel and sought,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4810">4810</a></font></span> It is a syknesse of the thought<br> <a name="an_4811"></a> Annexed and knet bitwixe tweyne,<br> <a name="an_4812"></a> Which male and female, with oo cheyne,<br> <a name="an_4813"></a> So frely byndith that they nyll twynne,<br> <a name="an_4814"></a> Whether so therof they leese or wynne.<br> <a name="an_4815"></a> The roote springith thurgh hoot brennyng<br> <a name="an_4816"></a> Into disordinat desiryng<br> <a name="an_4817"></a> For to kissen and enbrace,<br> <a name="an_4818"></a> And at her lust them to solace.<br> <a name="an_4819"></a> Of other thyng love recchith nought,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4820">4820</a></font></span> But setteth her herte and all her thought<br> <a name="an_4821"></a> More for delectacioun<br> <a name="an_4822"></a> Than ony procreacioun<br> <a name="an_4823"></a> Of other fruyt by engendring,<br> <a name="an_4824"></a> Which love to God is not plesyng;<br> <a name="an_4825"></a> For of her body fruyt to get<br> <a name="an_4826"></a> They yeve no force, they are so set<br> <a name="an_4827"></a> Upon delit to pley in-feere.<br> <a name="an_4828"></a> And somme have also this manere,<br> <a name="an_4829"></a> To feynen hem for love sek;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4830">4830</a></font></span> Sich love I preise not at a lek.<br> <a name="an_4831"></a> For paramours they do but feyne;<br> <a name="an_4832"></a> To love truly they disdeyne.<br> <a name="an_4833"></a> They falsen ladies traitoursly,<br> <a name="an_4834"></a> And swern hem othes utterly,<br> <a name="an_4835"></a> With many a lesyng and many a fable,<br> <a name="an_4836"></a> And all they fynden deceyvable.<br> <a name="an_4837"></a> And whanne they han her lust geten,<br> <a name="an_4838"></a> The hoote ernes they al foryeten.<br> <a name="an_4839"></a> Wymmen, the harm they bien full sore;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4840">4840</a></font></span> But men this thenken evermore,<br> <a name="an_4841"></a> That lasse harm is, so mote I the,<br> <a name="an_4842"></a> Deceyve them than deceyved be;<br> <a name="an_4843"></a> And namely, where they ne may<br> <a name="an_4844"></a> Fynde non other mene wey.<br> <a name="an_4845"></a> For I wot wel, in sothfastnesse,<br> <a name="an_4846"></a> [What man] doth now his bisynesse<br> <a name="an_4847"></a> With ony womman for to dele,<br> <a name="an_4848"></a> For ony lust that he may fele,<br> <a name="an_4849"></a> But if it be for engendrure,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4850">4850</a></font></span> He doth trespas, I you ensure.<br> <a name="an_4851"></a> For he shulde setten all his wil<br> <a name="an_4852"></a> To geten a likly thyng hym til,<br> <a name="an_4853"></a> And to sustene, if he myght,<br> <a name="an_4854"></a> And kepe forth, by Kyndes right,<br> <a name="an_4855"></a> His owne lyknesse and semblable;<br> <a name="an_4857"></a> And faile shulde successioun,<br> <a name="an_4858"></a> Ne were ther generacioun<br> <a name="an_4859"></a> Oure sectis strene for to save.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_4860">4860</a></font></span> Whanne fader or moder arn in grave,<br> <a name="an_4861"></a> Her children shulde, whanne they ben deede,<br> <a name="an_4862"></a> Full diligent ben, in her steede,<br> <a name="an_4863"></a> To use that werk on such a wise<br> <a name="an_4864"></a> That oon may thurgh another rise.<br> <a name="an_4865"></a> Therfore sette Kynde therynne delit,<br> <a name="an_4866"></a> For men therynne shulde hem delit,<br> <a pace<br> <a name="an_4893"></a> Withoute ony deth or distresse,<br> <a name="an_4894"></a> It is so full of wyldenesse,<br> <a name="an_4895"></a> So ofte it doth shame or damage<br> <a <a name="an_5043"></a> But if it be ony fool or nyce,<br> <a name="an_5044"></a> In whom that Shame hath no justice.<br> <a name="an_5045"></a> For to delyt echon they drawe,<br> <a class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5080">5080</a></font></span> And don al that they han ado,<br> <a name="an_5081"></a> As curteis shulde and debonaire,<br> <a name="an_5082"></a> And in her love beren hem faire,<br> <a name="an_5083"></a> Withoute vice, bothe he and she,<br> <a name="an_5084"></a> So that alwey, in honeste,<br> <a name="an_5085"></a> Fro foly love they kepe hem cler,<br> <a name="an_5086"></a> That brenneth hertis with his fer;<br> <a name="an_5087"></a> And that her love, in ony wise,<br> <a name="an_5088"></a> Be devoide of coveitise.<br> <a name="an_5089"></a> Good love shulde engendrid be<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5090">5090</a></font></span> Of trewe herte, just, and secre,<br> <a name="an_5091"></a> And not of such as sette her thought<br> <a name="an_5092"></a> To have her lust and ellis nought --<br> <a name="an_5093"></a> So are they caught in Loves las,<br> <a name="an_5094"></a> Truly, for bodily solas.<br> <a name="an_5095"></a> Fleshly delit is so present<br> <a name="an_5096"></a> With thee, that sette all thyn entent<br> <a name="an_5097"></a> Withoute more (what shulde I glose?)<br> <a name="an_5098"></a> For to gete and have the Rose,<br> <a name="an_5099"></a> Which makith [thee] so mat and wood<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5100">5100</a></font></span> That thou desirest noon other good.<br> <a name="an_5101"></a> But thou art not an inche the nerre,<br> <a name="an_5102"></a> But evere abidist in sorwe and werre,<br> <a name="an_5103"></a> As in thi face it is sene.<br> <a name="an_5104"></a> It makith thee bothe pale and lene;<br> <a name="an_5105"></a> Thy myght, thi vertu goth away.<br> <a name="an_5106"></a> A sory gest, in goode fay,<br> <a name="an_5107"></a> Thou herberest than in thyn inn,<br> <a name="an_5108"></a> The God of Love whanne thou let inn!<br> <a name="an_5109"></a> Wherfore I rede, thou shette hym oute,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5110">5110</a></font></span> Or he shall greve thee, out of doute;<br> <a name="an_5111"></a> For to thi profit it wol turne,<br> <a name="an_5112"></a> If he nomore with thee sojourne.<br> <a name="an_5113"></a> In gret myscheef and sorwe sonken<br> <a name="an_5114"></a> Ben hertis that of love arn dronken,<br> <a name="an_5115"></a> As thou peraventure knowen shall,<br> <a name="an_5116"></a> Whanne thou hast lost thy tyme all,<br> <a name="an_5117"></a> And spent thy youthe in ydilnesse,<br> <a name="an_5118"></a> In waste and wofull lustynesse.<br> <a name="an_5119"></a> If thou maist lyve the tyme to se<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5120">5120</a></font></span> Of love for to delyvered be,<br> <a name="an_5121"></a> Thy tyme thou shalt biwepe sore,<br> <a name="an_5122"></a> The whiche never thou maist restore;<br> <a name="an_5123"></a> For tyme lost, as men may see,<br> <a name="an_5124"></a> For nothyng may recured be.<br> <a name="an_5125"></a> And if thou scape yit, atte laste,<br> <a name="an_5126"></a> Fro Love, that hath thee so faste<br> <a name="an_5127"></a> Knytt and bounden in his las,<br> <a name="an_5128"></a> Certeyn I holde it but a gras.<br> <a name="an_5129"></a> For many oon, as it is seyn,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5130">5130</a></font></span> Have lost and spent also in veyn,<br> <a name="an_5131"></a> In his servise, withoute socour,<br> <a name="an_5132"></a> Body and soule, good and tresour,<br> <a name="an_5133"></a> Wit and strengthe, and eke richesse,<br> <a name="an_5134"></a> Of which they hadde never redresse."<br> <a name="an_5135"></a> L'amant Thus taught and preched hath<br> <a name="an_5136"></a> Resoun, but Love spilte hir sermoun,<br> <a name="an_5137"></a> That was so ymped in my thought,<br> <a name="an_5138"></a> That hir doctrine I sette at nought.<br> <a name="an_5139"></a> And yitt ne seide she never a del<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5140">5140</a></font></span> That I ne undirstod it wel,<br> <a name="an_5141"></a> Word by word, the mater all;<br> <a name="an_5142"></a> But unto Love I was so thrall,<br> <a name="an_5143"></a> Which callith overall his pray,<br> <a name="an_5144"></a> He chasith so my thought alway,<br> <a name="an_5145"></a> And holdith myn herte undir his sel<br> <a name="an_5146"></a> As trust and trew as ony stel;<br> <a name="an_5147"></a> So that no devocioun<br> <a name="an_5148"></a> Ne hadde I in the sermoun<br> <a name="an_5149"></a> Of dame Resoun, ne of hir red.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5150">5150</a></font></span> It tok no sojour in myn hed,<br> <a name="an_5151"></a> For all yede out at oon ere<br> <a name="an_5152"></a> That in that other she dide lere.<br> <a name="an_5153"></a> Fully on me she lost hir lore;<br> <a name="an_5154"></a> Hir speche me greved wondir sore.<br> <a name="an_5155"></a> Than unto hir for ire I seide,<br> <a name="an_5156"></a> For anger, as I dide abraide:<br> <a name="an_5157"></a> "Dame, and is it youre wille algate<br> <a name="an_5158"></a> That I not love, but that I hate<br> <a name="an_5159"></a> Alle men, as ye me teche?<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5160">5160</a></font></span> For if I do aftir youre speche,<br> <a name="an_5161"></a> Sith that ye seyn love is not good,<br> <a name="an_5162"></a> Thanne must I nedis ay with mood,<br> <a name="an_5163"></a> If I it leve, in hatrede ay<br> <a name="an_5164"></a> Lyven, and voide love away<br> <a name="an_5165"></a> From me, [and] [ben] a synfull wrecche<br> <a name="an_5166"></a> Hated of all [that] [love] that tecche.<br> <a name="an_5167"></a> I may not go noon other gate,<br> <a name="an_5168"></a> For other must I love or hate.<br> <a name="an_5169"></a> And if I hate men of-newe<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5170">5170</a></font></span> More than love, it wol me rewe,<br> <a name="an_5171"></a> As by youre preching semeth me,<br> <a name="an_5172"></a> For Love nothing ne preisith thee.<br> <a name="an_5173"></a> Ye yeve good counsel, sikirly,<br> <a name="an_5174"></a> That prechith me alday that I<br> <a name="an_5175"></a> Shulde not Loves lore alowe.<br> <a name="an_5176"></a> He were a fool, wolde you not trowe!<br> <a name="an_5177"></a> In speche also ye han me taught<br> <a name="an_5178"></a> Another love, that knowen is naught,<br> <a name="an_5179"></a> Which I have herd you not repreve,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a By youre leve,<br> <a name="an_5181"></a> If ye wolde diffyne it me,<br> <a name="an_5182"></a> I wolde gladly here, to se,<br> <a name="an_5183"></a> At the leest, if I may lere<br> <a name="an_5184"></a> Of sondry loves the manere."<br> <a name="an_5185"></a> Raisoun "Certis, freend, a fool art thou,<br> <a name="an_5186"></a> Whan that thou nothyng wolt allow<br> <a name="an_5187"></a> That I for thi profit say.<br> <a name="an_5188"></a> Yit wole I sey thee more in fay,<br> <a name="an_5189"></a> For I am redy, at the leste,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5190">5190</a></font></span> To accomplisshe thi requeste.<br> <a name="an_5191"></a> But I not where it wole avayle;<br> <a name="an_5192"></a> In veyn, perauntre, I shal travayle.<br> <a name="an_5193"></a> Love ther is in sondry wise,<br> <a name="an_5194"></a> As I shal thee heere devise.<br> <a name="an_5195"></a> For som love leful is and good --<br> <a name="an_5196"></a> I mene not that which makith thee wood,<br> <a name="an_5197"></a> And bringith thee in many a fit,<br> <a name="an_5198"></a> And ravysshith fro thee al thi wit,<br> <a name="an_5199"></a> It is so merveilous and queynt;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5200">5200</a></font></span> With such love be no more aqueynt.<br> <a name="an_5201"></a> "Love of freendshipp also ther is,<br> <a name="an_5202"></a> Which makith no man don amys,<br> <a name="an_5203"></a> Of wille knytt bitwixe two,<br> <a name="an_5204"></a> That wole not breke for wele ne woo;<br> <a name="an_5205"></a> Which long is likly to contune,<br> <a name="an_5206"></a> Whanne wille and goodis ben in comune;<br> <a name="an_5207"></a> Grounded by Goddis ordinaunce,<br> <a name="an_5208"></a> Hool, withoute discordaunce;<br> <a name="an_5209"></a> With hem holdyng comunte<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5213"></a> That ech helpe other at her neede,<br> <a name="an_5214"></a> And wisely hele bothe word and dede;<br> <a name="an_5215"></a> Trewe of menyng, devoide of slouthe,<br> <a class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5230">5230</a></font></span> For if his freend, thurgh ony gate,<br> <a name="an_5231"></a> Wole compleyne of his poverte,<br> <a name="an_5232"></a> He shulde not bide so long til he<br> <a name="an_5233"></a> Of his helpyng hym requere;<br> <a name="an_5234"></a> For good dede, don thurgh praiere,<br> <a name="an_5235"></a> Is sold and bought to deere, iwys,<br> <a name="an_5236"></a> To hert that of gret valour is.<br> <a name="an_5237"></a> For hert fulfilled of gentilnesse<br> <a name="an_5238"></a> Can yvel demene his distresse;<br> <a name="an_5239"></a> And man that worthy is of name<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5240">5240</a></font></span> To asken often hath gret shame.<br> <a name="an_5241"></a> A good man brenneth in his thought<br> <a name="an_5242"></a> For shame, whanne he axeth ought.<br> <a name="an_5243"></a> He hath gret thought and dredeth ay<br> <a name="an_5244"></a> For his disese, whanne he shal pray<br> <a name="an_5245"></a> His freend, lest that he warned be,<br> <a name="an_5246"></a> Til that he preve his stabilte.<br> <a nought;<br> <a name="an_5259"></a> For tweyne of noumbre is bet than thre<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5260">5260</a></font></span> In every counsell and secre.<br> <a name="an_5261"></a> Repreve he dredeth never a deel,<br> <a name="an_5262"></a> Who that bisett his wordis wel;<br> <a name="an_5263"></a> For every wise man, out of drede,<br> <a name="an_5264"></a> Can kepe his tunge til he se nede;<br> <a name="an_5265"></a> And fooles can not holde her tunge;<br> <a name="an_5266"></a> A fooles belle is soone runge.<br> <a felow, for that he<br> <a name="an_5276"></a> May not fulfille his volunte<br> <a name="an_5277"></a> Fully, as he hath requered.<br> <a name="an_5278"></a> If bothe the hertis Love hath fered,<br> <a name="an_5284"></a> If love wel departed be.<br> <a name="an_5285"></a> "And whilom of this amyte<br> <a name="an_5286"></a> Spak Tulius in a ditee:<br> <a name="an_5287"></a> `Man shulde maken his request<br> <a name="an_5288"></a> Unto his freend, that is honest;<br> <a name="an_5289"></a> And he goodly shulde it fulfille,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5301"></a> In thise two caas with his myght,<br> <a name="an_5302"></a> Taking no kep to skile nor right,<br> <a name="an_5303"></a> As fer as love may hym excuse,<br> <a size="-1"><a name="an_5310">5310</a></font></span> The tothir fooles blent and shendith.<br> <a name="an_5311"></a> "Another love also there is<br> <a name="an_5312"></a> That is contrarie unto this,<br> <a name="an_5313"></a> Which desir is so constreyned<br> <a name="an_5314"></a> That [it] is but wille feyned.<br> <a name="an_5315"></a> Awey fro trouthe it doth so varie<br> <a name="an_5316"></a> That to good love it is contrarie;<br> <a name="an_5317"></a> For it maymeth, in many wise,<br> <a name="an_5318"></a> Sike hertis with coveitise.<br> <a name="an_5319"></a> All in balaunce<br> <a name="an_5322"></a> That, if it lese his hope, perchaunce,<br> <a name="an_5323"></a> Of lucre, that he is sett upon,<br> <a name="an_5324"></a> It wole faile and quenche anoon;<br> <a name="an_5325"></a> For no man may be amerous,<br> <a name="an_5326"></a> Ne in his lyvyng vertuous,<br> <a name="an_5327"></a> But he love more, in mood,<br> <a name="an_5328"></a> Men for hemsilf than for her good.<br> <a name="an_5329"></a> For love that profit doth abide<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5330">5330</a></font></span> Is fals, and bit not in no tyde.<br> <a name="an_5331"></a> [This] love cometh of dame Fortune,<br> <a name="an_5332"></a> That litel while wol contune;<br> <a name="an_5333"></a> For it shal chaungen wonder soone,<br> <a name="an_5334"></a> And take eclips, right as the moone,<br> <a name="an_5335"></a> Whanne she is from us lett<br> <a name="an_5336"></a> Thurgh erthe, that bitwixe is sett<br> <a name="an_5337"></a> The sonne and hir, as it may fall,<br> <a name="an_5338"></a> Be it in partie, or in all.<br> <a name="an_5339"></a> The shadowe maketh her bemys merke,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5340">5340</a></font></span> And hir hornes to shewe derke,<br> <a name="an_5341"></a> That part where she hath lost hir lyght<br> <a name="an_5342"></a> Of Phebus fully, and the sight;<br> <a name="an_5343"></a> Til, whanne the shadowe is overpast,<br> <a name="an_5344"></a> She is enlumyned ageyn as fast,<br> <a name="an_5345"></a> Thurgh the brightnesse of the sonne bemes,<br> <a name="an_5346"></a> That yeveth to hir ageyn hir lemes.<br> <a name="an_5347"></a> That love is right of sich nature;<br> <a name="an_5348"></a> Now is faire, and now obscure,<br> <a name="an_5349"></a> Now bright, now clipsi of manere,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5350">5350</a></font></span> And whilom dym, and whilom clere.<br> <a name="an_5351"></a> As soone as Poverte gynneth take,<br> <a name="an_5352"></a> With mantel and wedis blake<br> <a name="an_5353"></a> Hidith of love the light awey,<br> <a name="an_5354"></a> That into nyght it turneth day,<br> <a name="an_5355"></a> It may not see Richesse shyne<br> <a name="an_5356"></a> Till the blak shadowes fyne.<br> <a name="an_5357"></a> For, whanne Richesse shyneth bright,<br> <a name="an_5358"></a> Love recovereth ageyn his light;<br> <a name="an_5359"></a> And whanne it failith he wol flit,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5360">5360</a></font></span> And as she groweth, so groweth it.<br> <a name="an_5361"></a> Of this love -- here what I sey! --<br> <a name="an_5362"></a> The riche men are loved ay,<br> <a name="an_5363"></a> And namely tho that sparand ben,<br> <a name="an_5364"></a> That wole not wasshe her hertes clen<br> <a name="an_5365"></a> Of the filthe nor of the vice<br> <a name="an_5366"></a> Of gredy brennyng avarice.<br> <a name="an_5367"></a> The riche man full fonned is, ywys,<br> <a name="an_5368"></a> That weneth that he loved is.<br> <a name="an_5369"></a> If that his herte it undirstod,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5370">5370</a></font></span> It is not he, it is his good;<br> <a name="an_5371"></a> He may wel witen in his thought,<br> <a name="an_5372"></a> His good is loved, and he right nought.<br> <a name="an_5373"></a> For if he be a nygard ek,<br> <a name="an_5374"></a> Men wole not sette by hym a lek,<br> <a name="an_5375"></a> But haten hym; this is the soth.<br> <a name="an_5376"></a> Lo, what profit his catell doth.<br> <a name="an_5377"></a> Of every man that may hym see<br> <a name="an_5378"></a> It geteth hym nought but enmyte.<br> <a name="an_5379"></a> But he amende hym of that vice,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5380">5380</a></font></span> And knowe hymsilf, he is not wys.<br> <a name="an_5381"></a> Certys, he shulde ay freendly be,<br> <a name="an_5382"></a> To gete hym love also ben free,<br> <a name="an_5383"></a> Or ellis he is not wise ne sage<br> <a name="an_5384"></a> Nomore than is a goot ramage.<br> <a name="an_5385"></a> That he not loveth, his dede proveth,<br> <a name="an_5386"></a> Whan he his richesse so wel loveth<br> <a name="an_5387"></a> That he wole hide it ay and spare,<br> <a name="an_5388"></a> His pore freendis sen forfare,<br> <a name="an_5389"></a> To kepen ay his purpos,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5390">5390</a></font></span> Til for drede his yen clos,<br> <a name="an_5391"></a> And til a wikked deth hym take.<br> <a name="an_5392"></a> Hym hadde lever asondre shake,<br> <a name="an_5393"></a> And late alle his lymes asondre ryve,<br> <a name="an_5394"></a> Than leve his richesse in his lyve.<br> <a name="an_5395"></a> He thenkith parte it with no man;<br> <a name="an_5396"></a> Certayn, no love is in hym than.<br> <a name="an_5397"></a> How shulde love withynne hym be,<br> <a name="an_5398"></a> Whanne in his herte is no pite?<br> <a name="an_5399"></a> That he trespasseth, wel I wat,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5400">5400</a></font></span> For ech man knowith his estat;<br> <a name="an_5401"></a> For wel hym ought to be reproved<br> <a name="an_5402"></a> That loveth nought, ne is not loved.<br> <a name="an_5403"></a> "But sith we arn to Fortune comen,<br> <a name="an_5404"></a> And han oure sermoun of hir nomen,<br> <a name="an_5408"></a> Though sothfastnesse it be all,<br> <a name="an_5409"></a> As it is writen, and is soth,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5413"></a> And if thee thynke it is doutable,<br> <a name="an_5414"></a> It is thurgh argument provable;<br> <a name="an_5415"></a> For the debonaire and softe<br> <a name="an_5416"></a> Falsith and bigilith ofte;<br> <a name="an_5417"></a> For lyche a moder she can cherish,<br> <a name="an_5418"></a> And mylken as doth a norys,<br> <a name="an_5419"></a> And of name="an_5650">5650</a></font></span> In a book that `The Golden Verses'<br> <a name="an_5651"></a> Is clepid, for the nobilite<br> <a name="an_5652"></a> Of the honourable ditee: --<br> <a name="an_5653"></a> `Thanne, whanne thou gost thy body fro,<br> <a name="an_5654"></a> Fre in the eir thou shalt up go,<br> <a name="an_5655"></a> And leven al humanite,<br> <a name="an_5656"></a> And purely lyve in deite.'<br> <a name="an_5657"></a> He is a fool, withouten were,<br> <a name="an_5658"></a> That trowith have his countre heere.<br> <a name="an_5659"></a> `In erthe is not oure countre,'<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5660">5660</a></font></span> That may these clerkis seyn and see<br> <a name="an_5661"></a> In Boece of Consolacioun,<br> <a name="an_5662"></a> Where it is maked mencioun<br> <a name="an_5663"></a> Of oure contre pleyn at the ye,<br> <a name="an_5664"></a> By teching of Philosophie,<br> <a name="an_5665"></a> Where lewid men myght lere wit,<br> <a name="an_5666"></a> Whoso that wolde translaten it.<br> <a name="an_5667"></a> If he be sich that can wel lyve<br> <a name="an_5668"></a> Aftir his rente may hym yive,<br> <a name="an_5669"></a> And not desireth more to have<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5670">5670</a></font></span> Than may fro poverte hym save,<br> <a name="an_5671"></a> A wise man seide, as we may seen,<br> <a name="an_5672"></a> Is no man wrecched, but he it wen,<br> <a name="an_5673"></a> Be he kyng, knyght, or ribaud.<br> <a name="an_5674"></a> And many a ribaud is mery and baud,<br> <a name="an_5675"></a> That swynkith, and berith, bothe day and nyght,<br> <a name="an_5676"></a> Many a burthen of gret myght,<br> <a name="an_5677"></a> The whiche doth hym lasse offense<br> <a name="an_5678"></a> For he suffrith in pacience.<br> <a name="an_5679"></a> They laugh and daunce, trippe and synge,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5680">5680</a></font></span> And ley not up for her lyvynge,<br> <a name="an_5681"></a> But in the taverne all dispendith<br> <a name="an_5682"></a> The wynnyng that God hem sendith.<br> <a name="an_5683"></a> Thanne goth he, fardeles for to ber<br> <a name="an_5684"></a> With as good chere as he dide er.<br> <a name="an_5685"></a> To swynke and traveile he not feynith,<br> <a name="an_5686"></a> For for to robben he disdeynith.<br> <a name="an_5687"></a> But right anoon aftir his swynk<br> <a name="an_5688"></a> He goth to taverne for to drynk.<br> <a name="an_5689"></a> All these ar riche in abundaunce<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5690">5690</a></font></span> That can thus have suffisaunce<br> <a name="an_5691"></a> Wel more than can an usurere,<br> <a name="an_5692"></a> As God wel knowith, withoute were.<br> <a name="an_5693"></a> For an usurer, so God me se,<br> <a name="an_5694"></a> Shal nevere for richesse riche be,<br> <a name="an_5695"></a> But evermore pore and indigent,<br> <a name="an_5696"></a> Scarce and gredy in his entent.<br> <a name="an_5697"></a> "For soth it is, whom it displese,<br> <a name="an_5698"></a> Ther may no marchaunt lyve at ese;<br> <a name="an_5699"></a> His herte in sich a were is sett<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5700">5700</a></font></span> That it quyk brenneth [more] to get,<br> <a name="an_5701"></a> Ne never shal ynogh have geten,<br> <a name="an_5702"></a> Though he have gold in gerners yeten,<br> <a name="an_5703"></a> For to be nedy he dredith sore.<br> <a name="an_5704"></a> Wherfore to geten more and more<br> <a name="an_5705"></a> He set his herte and his desir;<br> <a name="an_5706"></a> So hote he brennyth in the fir<br> <a name="an_5707"></a> Of coveitise, that makith hym wood<br> <a name="an_5708"></a> To purchace other mennes good.<br> <a name="an_5709"></a> He undirfongith a gret peyne,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5710">5710</a></font></span> That undirtakith to drynke up Seyne;<br> <a name="an_5711"></a> For the more he drynkith, ay<br> <a name="an_5712"></a> The more he leveth, the soth to say.<br> <a name="an_5713"></a> Thus is thurst of fals getyng,<br> <a name="an_5714"></a> That last ever in coveityng,<br> <a name="an_5715"></a> And the angwisshe and distresse<br> <a name="an_5716"></a> With the fir of gredynesse.<br> <a name="an_5717"></a> She fightith with hym ay, and stryveth,<br> <a name="an_5718"></a> That his herte asondre ryveth.<br> <a name="an_5719"></a> Such gredynesse hym assaylith<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5720">5720</a></font></span> That whanne he most hath, most he failith.<br> <a name="an_5721"></a> Phisiciens and advocates<br> <a name="an_5722"></a> Gon right by the same yates;<br> <a name="an_5723"></a> They selle her science for wynnyng,<br> <a name="an_5724"></a> And haunte her craft for gret getyng.<br> <a name="an_5725"></a> Her wynnyng is of such swetnesse<br> <a name="an_5726"></a> That if a man falle in siknesse,<br> <a name="an_5727"></a> They are full glad for her encres;<br> <a name="an_5728"></a> For by her wille, withoute lees,<br> <a name="an_5729"></a> Everich man shulde be sek,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5730">5730</a></font></span> And though they die, they sette not a lek.<br> <a name="an_5731"></a> After, whanne they the gold have take,<br> <a name="an_5732"></a> Full litel care for hem they make.<br> <a name="an_5733"></a> They wolde that fourty were seke at onys,<br> <a name="an_5734"></a> Ye, two hundred, in flesh and bonys,<br> <a name="an_5735"></a> And yit two thousand, as I gesse,<br> <a name="an_5736"></a> For to encrecen her richesse.<br> <a name="an_5737"></a> They wole not worchen, in no wise,<br> <a name="an_5738"></a> But for lucre and coveitise.<br> <a name="an_5739"></a> For fysic gynneth first by fy,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5740">5740</a></font></span> The physicien also sothely;<br> <a name="an_5741"></a> And sithen it goth fro fy to sy:<br> <a name="an_5742"></a> To truste on hem is foly;<br> <a name="an_5743"></a> For they nyl, in no maner gre,<br> <a name="an_5744"></a> Do right nought for charite.<br> <a name="an_5745"></a> "Eke in the same secte ar sett<br> <a name="an_5746"></a> All tho that prechen for to get<br> <a name="an_5747"></a> Worshipes, honour, and richesse.<br> <a name="an_5748"></a> Her hertis arn in gret distresse<br> <a name="an_5749"></a> That folk lyve not holily.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5750">5750</a></font></span> But aboven all, specialy,<br> <a name="an_5751"></a> Sich as prechen [for] veynglorie,<br> <a name="an_5752"></a> And toward God have no memorie,<br> <a name="an_5753"></a> But forth as ypocrites trace,<br> <a name="an_5754"></a> And to her soules deth purchace,<br> <a name="an_5755"></a> And outward shewen holynesse,<br> <a name="an_5756"></a> Though they be full of cursidnesse.<br> <a name="an_5757"></a> Not liche to the apostles twelve,<br> <a name="an_5758"></a> They deceyve other and hemselve.<br> <a name="an_5759"></a> Bigiled is the giler than,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5760">5760</a></font></span> For prechyng of a cursed man,<br> <a name="an_5761"></a> Though [it] to other may profite,<br> <a name="an_5762"></a> Hymsilf it availeth not a myte;<br> <a name="an_5763"></a> For ofte good predicacioun<br> <a name="an_5764"></a> Cometh of evel entencioun.<br> <a name="an_5765"></a> To hym not vailith his preching,<br> <a name="an_5766"></a> All helpe he other with his teching;<br> <a name="an_5767"></a> For where they good ensaumple take,<br> <a name="an_5768"></a> There is he with veynglorie shake.<br> <a name="an_5769"></a> "But late us leven these prechoures,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5770">5770</a></font></span> And speke of hem that in her toures<br> <a name="an_5771"></a> Hepe up hir gold, and faste shette,<br> <a name="an_5772"></a> And sore theron her herte sette.<br> <a name="an_5773"></a> They neither love God ne drede;<br> <a name="an_5774"></a> They kepe more than it is nede,<br> <a name="an_5775"></a> And in her bagges sore it bynde,<br> <a name="an_5776"></a> Out of the sonne and of the wynde.<br> <a name="an_5777"></a> They putte up more than nede ware,<br> <a name="an_5778"></a> Whanne they seen pore folk forfare,<br> <a name="an_5779"></a> For hunger die, and for cold quake.<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5780">5780</a></font></span> God can wel vengeaunce therof take!<br> <a name="an_5781"></a> Three gret myscheves hem assailith,<br> <a name="an_5782"></a> And thus in gadring ay travaylith.<br> <a name="an_5783"></a> With myche peyne they wynne richesse;<br> <a name="an_5784"></a> And drede hem holdith in distresse<br> <a name="an_5785"></a> To kepe that they gadre faste;<br> <a name="an_5786"></a> With sorwe they leve it at the laste.<br> <a name="an_5787"></a> With sorwe they bothe dye and lyve,<br> <a name="an_5788"></a> That unto richesse her hertis yive;<br> <a name="an_5789"></a> And in defaute of love it is,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5790">5790</a></font></span> As it shewith ful wel, iwys.<br> <a name="an_5791"></a> For if thise gredy, the sothe to seyn,<br> <a name="an_5792"></a> Loveden and were loved ageyn,<br> <a name="an_5793"></a> And good love regned overall,<br> <a name="an_5794"></a> Such wikkidnesse ne shulde fall;<br> <a name="an_5795"></a> But he shulde yeve that most good had<br> <a name="an_5796"></a> To hem that weren in nede bistad,<br> <a name="an_5797"></a> And lyve withoute false usure,<br> <a name="an_5798"></a> For charite full clene and pure.<br> <a name="an_5799"></a> If they hem yeve to goodnesse,<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5800">5800</a></font></span> Defendyng hem from ydelnesse,<br> <a name="an_5801"></a> In all this world thanne pore noon<br> <a name="an_5802"></a> We shulde fynde, I trowe, not oon.<br> <a name="an_5803"></a> But chaunged is this world unstable,<br> <a name="an_5804"></a> For love is overall vendable.<br> <a name="an_5805"></a> We se that no man loveth now,<br> <a name="an_5806"></a> But for wynnyng and for prow;<br> <a name="an_5807"></a> And love is thralled in servage,<br> <a name="an_5808"></a> Whanne it is sold for avauntage.<br> <a name="an_5809"></a> Yit wommen wole her bodyes selle;<br> <span class="margnote"><font color="GREEN" size="-1"><a name="an_5810">5810</a></font></span> Suche soules goth to the devel of helle!"<br>
